            <td>719.1&nbsp;km<sup><small>2</small></sup><sup id="cite_ref-singstat2015pop.26land_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singstat2015pop.26land-10">[9]</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area" title="List of countries and dependencies by area" class="mw-redirect">190th</a>)<br> 278&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi</td> 
           </tr>

     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:1_singapore_f1_night_race_2012_city_skyline.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/1_singapore_f1_night_race_2012_city_skyline.jpg/290px-1_singapore_f1_night_race_2012_city_skyline.jpg" width="290" height="194" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/1_singapore_f1_night_race_2012_city_skyline.jpg/435px-1_singapore_f1_night_race_2012_city_skyline.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/1_singapore_f1_night_race_2012_city_skyline.jpg/580px-1_singapore_f1_night_race_2012_city_skyline.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1367"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:1_singapore_f1_night_race_2012_city_skyline.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Grand_Prix" title="Singapore Grand Prix">Singapore Grand Prix</a> – 
        <a href="/wiki/F1" title="F1" class="mw-redirect">F1's</a> first night race, at 
        <a href="/wiki/Marina_Bay,_Singapore" title="Marina Bay, Singapore">Marina Bay</a> street circuit. Pop concerts at the 
        <a href="/wiki/Padang,_Singapore" title="Padang, Singapore">Padang</a> centre field are a major part of its F1 experience
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><b>Singapore</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="noexcerpt"><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/36/En-us-Singapore.ogg" title="Listen"><img alt="Listen" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/11px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/17px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/22px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="11" data-file-height="11"></a><sup><span class="IPA" style="color:#00e;font:bold 80% sans-serif;padding:0 .1em"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Singapore.ogg" title="File:En-us-Singapore.ogg">i</a></span></sup></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/ɪ/ short 'i' in 'bid'">ɪ</span><span title="/ŋɡ/ 'ng' in 'finger'">ŋɡ</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/ɔːr/ 'or' in 'born'">ɔːr</span></span>/</a></span></span>), officially the <b>Republic of Singapore</b>, and often referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Singapore#Etymology" title="Singapore"><i>Lion City</i>, the <i>Garden City</i>, and the <i>Red Dot</i></a>, is a <a href="/wiki/Global_city" title="Global city">global city</a> in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> and the world's only <a href="/wiki/Island_country" title="Island country">island</a> <a href="/wiki/City-state" title="City-state">city-state</a>. It lies <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">one degree</a> (137&nbsp;km) north of the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">equator</a>, at the southernmost tip of <a href="/wiki/Continental_Asia" title="Continental Asia" class="mw-redirect">continental Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_Malaysia" title="Peninsular Malaysia">peninsular Malaysia</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Riau_Islands" title="Riau Islands">Riau Islands</a> to the south. Singapore's territory consists of the diamond-shaped main island and 62 <a href="/wiki/Islet" title="Islet">islets</a>. Since <a href="/wiki/Independence" title="Independence">independence</a>, extensive <a href="/wiki/Land_reclamation" title="Land reclamation">land reclamation</a> has increased its total size by 23% (130&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>), and its <a href="/wiki/National_Parks_Board" title="National Parks Board">greening policy</a> has covered the <a href="/wiki/Densely_populated" title="Densely populated" class="mw-redirect">densely populated</a> island with <a href="/wiki/Tropics" title="Tropics">tropical</a> <a href="/wiki/Flora" title="Flora">flora</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_parks_in_Singapore" title="List of parks in Singapore">parks and gardens</a>.</p> 
     <p>The islands were settled from the second century <a href="/wiki/AD" title="AD" class="mw-redirect">AD</a> by a <a href="/wiki/Early_history_of_Singapore" title="Early history of Singapore">series of local empires</a>. In 1819, <a href="/wiki/Sir_Stamford_Raffles" title="Sir Stamford Raffles" class="mw-redirect">Sir Stamford Raffles</a> <a href="/wiki/Founding_of_modern_Singapore" title="Founding of modern Singapore">founded modern Singapore</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Trading_post" title="Trading post">trading post</a> of the <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">East India Company</a>; after the company collapsed, the islands were ceded to <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">Britain</a> and became part of its <a href="/wiki/Straits_Settlements" title="Straits Settlements">Straits Settlements</a> in 1826. During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Singapore was <a href="/wiki/Japanese_occupation_of_Singapore" title="Japanese occupation of Singapore">occupied by Japan</a>. It gained independence from Britain in 1963, by uniting with other former British territories to form <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, but was expelled two years later over <a href="/wiki/Singapore_in_Malaysia" title="Singapore in Malaysia">ideological differences</a>. After early years of <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Republic_of_Singapore#1965_to_1979" title="History of the Republic of Singapore">turbulence</a>, and despite lacking <a href="/wiki/Natural_resources" title="Natural resources" class="mw-redirect">natural resources</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Hinterland" title="Hinterland">hinterland</a>, the nation developed rapidly as an <a href="/wiki/Four_Asian_Tigers" title="Four Asian Tigers">Asian Tiger</a> economy, based on <a href="/wiki/External_trade" title="External trade" class="mw-redirect">external trade</a> and its <a href="/wiki/Human_capital" title="Human capital">human capital</a>.</p> 
     <p>Singapore is a global commerce, finance and transport hub. Its standings include: "<a href="/wiki/Easiest_place_to_do_business" title="Easiest place to do business" class="mw-redirect">easiest place to do business</a>" (<a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>) for ten consecutive years, most <a href="/wiki/Global_Information_Technology_Report" title="Global Information Technology Report" class="mw-redirect">"technology-ready"</a> nation <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">(WEF)</a>, top <a href="/wiki/Union_of_International_Associations" title="Union of International Associations">"International meetings city" (UIA)</a>, city with "best investment potential" (BERI), 2nd-<a href="/wiki/Global_Competitiveness_Report" title="Global Competitiveness Report">most competitive country</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">(WEF)</a>, 3rd-largest <a href="/wiki/Foreign_exchange_market" title="Foreign exchange market">foreign exchange</a> centre, 4th-largest <a href="/wiki/Financial_centre" title="Financial centre">financial centre</a>, 3rd-largest <a href="/wiki/Oil_refining" title="Oil refining" class="mw-redirect">oil refining</a> and <a href="/wiki/Commodity_market" title="Commodity market">trading</a> centre and one of the top two <a href="/wiki/List_of_world%27s_busiest_container_ports" title="List of world's busiest container ports">busiest container ports</a> since the 1990s. Singapore's best known global brands include <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Airlines" title="Singapore Airlines">Singapore Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Changi_Airport" title="Changi Airport" class="mw-redirect">Changi Airport</a>, both amongst the most-awarded in their industry; <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Airlines" title="Singapore Airlines">SIA</a> is also rated by <a href="/wiki/Fortune_(magazine)" title="Fortune (magazine)"><i>Fortune</i></a> surveys as Asia's "most admired company". For the past decade, it has been the only Asian country with the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_credit_rating" title="List of countries by credit rating">top AAA sovereign rating</a> from all major <a href="/wiki/Credit_rating_agencies" title="Credit rating agencies" class="mw-redirect">credit rating agencies</a>, including <a href="/wiki/S%26P" title="S&amp;P" class="mw-redirect">S&amp;P</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moody%27s" title="Moody's" class="mw-redirect">Moody's</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fitch_Ratings" title="Fitch Ratings">Fitch</a>.</p> 
     <p>Singapore ranks high on its national <a href="/wiki/Social_policies" title="Social policies" class="mw-redirect">social policies</a>, leading Asia and 11th globally, on the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">(UN)</a>, notably on <a href="/wiki/International_rankings_of_Singapore" title="International rankings of Singapore">key measures</a> of <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Singapore" title="Education in Singapore">education</a>, <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Singapore" title="Healthcare in Singapore">healthcare</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_life_expectancy" title="List of countries by life expectancy">life expectancy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercer_Quality_of_Living_Survey" title="Mercer Quality of Living Survey">quality of life</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_intentional_homicide_rate" title="List of countries by intentional homicide rate">personal safety</a>, housing. Although income inequality is high, <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_home_ownership_rate" title="List of countries by home ownership rate">90% of citizens own their homes</a>, and the country has one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">highest per capita incomes</a>, with <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_tax_rates" title="List of countries by tax rates">low taxes</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Cosmopolitanism" title="Cosmopolitanism">cosmopolitan</a> nation is home to 5.5 million residents, 38% of whom are <a href="/wiki/Permanent_residency" title="Permanent residency">permanent residents</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Foreign_nationals" title="Foreign nationals" class="mw-redirect">foreign nationals</a>. Singaporeans are mostly <a href="/wiki/Bilingual" title="Bilingual" class="mw-redirect">bilingual</a>, with <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> as their common language and a second <a href="/wiki/Mother-tongue" title="Mother-tongue" class="mw-redirect">mother-tongue</a> language. Its <a href="/wiki/Cultural_diversity" title="Cultural diversity">cultural diversity</a> is reflected in its extensive <a href="/wiki/Singaporean_cuisine" title="Singaporean cuisine">"hawker" cuisine</a> and major ethnic <a href="/wiki/Festivals" title="Festivals" class="mw-redirect">festivals</a>—<a href="/wiki/Chinese_Singaporean" title="Chinese Singaporean" class="mw-redirect">Chinese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malays_in_Singapore" title="Malays in Singapore" class="mw-redirect">Malay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indians_in_Singapore" title="Indians in Singapore" class="mw-redirect">Indian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western</a>—which are all <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Singapore" title="Public holidays in Singapore">national holidays</a>. In 2015, <a href="/wiki/Lonely_Planet" title="Lonely Planet">Lonely Planet</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a> listed Singapore as their top and 6th best world destination to visit respectively.</p> 
     <p>The nation's core principles are <a href="/wiki/Meritocracy" title="Meritocracy">meritocracy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Multiculturalism" title="Multiculturalism">multiculturalism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Secularism" title="Secularism">secularism</a>. It is noted for its effective, <a href="/wiki/Realpolitik" title="Realpolitik">pragmatic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Corruption_Perceptions_Index" title="Corruption Perceptions Index">incorrupt</a> governance and <a href="/wiki/Civil_service" title="Civil service">civil service</a>, which together with its rapid development policies, is widely cited as the "Singapore model". <a href="/wiki/Gallup_(company)" title="Gallup (company)">Gallup</a> polls shows 84% of its residents expressed confidence in the national government, and 85% in its judicial systems—one of the highest ratings recorded. Singapore has significant influence on global affairs relative to its size, leading some analysts to classify it as a <a href="/wiki/Middle_power" title="Middle power">middle power</a>. It is ranked as Asia's most influential city and 4th in the world by <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i>.</p> 
     <p>Singapore is a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a> <a href="/wiki/Multiparty" title="Multiparty" class="mw-redirect">multiparty</a> <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">parliamentary republic</a>, with a <a href="/wiki/Westminster_system" title="Westminster system">Westminster system</a> of <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">unicameral</a> parliamentary government. The <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Action_Party" title="People's Action Party">People's Action Party</a> has won every election since self-government in 1959. One of the five founding members of the <a href="/wiki/ASEAN" title="ASEAN" class="mw-redirect">ASEAN</a>, Singapore is also the host of the <a href="/wiki/Asia-Pacific_Economic_Cooperation" title="Asia-Pacific Economic Cooperation">Asia-Pacific Economic Cooperation</a> (APEC) Secretariat, and a member of the <a href="/wiki/East_Asia_Summit" title="East Asia Summit">East Asia Summit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>.</p> 
     <p></p>

        </ul> </li> 
       <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#Geography"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Geography</span></a>
