     <p></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Names_of_Singapore" title="Names of Singapore">Names of Singapore</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The English name of Singapore is derived from the <a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">Malay</a> word, <i><span lang="ms" xml:lang="ms">Singapura</span></i>, which was in turn derived from <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> (Singa is "lion", Pura "city"; <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a>: <a href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E0%A4%B8%E0%A4%BF%E0%A4%82%E0%A4%B9%E0%A4%AA%E0%A5%81%E0%A4%B0" class="extiw" title="wikt:सिंहपुर">सिंहपुर</a>, <small><a href="/wiki/International_Alphabet_of_Sanskrit_Transliteration" title="International Alphabet of Sanskrit Transliteration">IAST</a></small>: <i>Siṃhápura</i>), hence the customary reference to the nation as the <i>Lion City</i>, and its inclusion in many of the nation's symbols (e.g., its coat of arms, Merlion emblem). However, it is unlikely that <a href="/wiki/Lion" title="Lion">lions</a> ever lived on the island; <a href="/wiki/Sang_Nila_Utama" title="Sang Nila Utama">Sang Nila Utama</a>, who founded and named the island <i>Singapura</i>, most likely saw a <a href="/wiki/Malayan_tiger" title="Malayan tiger">Malayan tiger</a>. It is also known as <i><a href="/wiki/Pulau_Ujong" title="Pulau Ujong">Pulau Ujong</a></i>, as far back as the 3rd century, literally 'island at the end' (of the <a href="/wiki/Malay_Peninsula" title="Malay Peninsula">Malay Peninsula</a>) in Malay.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Since the 1970s, Singapore has also been widely known as the <i>Garden City</i>, owing to its extensive greening policy covering the whole island, a priority of its first prime minister <a href="/wiki/Lee_Kuan_Yew" title="Lee Kuan Yew">Lee Kuan Yew</a>, dubbed the nation's "Chief Gardener". The nation's conservation and greening efforts contributed to <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Botanic_Gardens" title="Singapore Botanic Gardens">Singapore Botanic Gardens</a> being the only <a href="/wiki/Tropical_garden" title="Tropical garden">tropical garden</a> to be inscribed by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> as a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>. The nickname, <a href="/wiki/Little_Red_Dot" title="Little Red Dot" class="mw-redirect"><i>Red Dot</i></a>, is a reference to its size on the map, contrasting with its achievements. In 2015, Singapore's <a href="/wiki/Golden_Jubilee" title="Golden Jubilee" class="mw-redirect">Golden Jubilee</a> year, the celebratory "SG50" branding is depicted inside a red dot.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_Singapore" title="History of Singapore">History of Singapore</a>
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Temasek" title="Temasek">Temasek</a> ('Sea Town' in the Malay language), an outpost of the <a href="/wiki/Sumatra" title="Sumatra">Sumatran</a> <a href="/wiki/Srivijaya" title="Srivijaya">Srivijaya</a> empire, is the earliest written record relating to the area now called Singapore. In the 13th century, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Singapura" title="Kingdom of Singapura">Kingdom of Singapura</a> was established on the island and it became a trading port city. However, there were two major foreign invasions before it was destroyed by the Majapahit in 1398.<sup id="cite_ref-Tsang_2011_120_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tsang_2011_120-6">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-harvnb.7CSabrizain_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-harvnb.7CSabrizain-4">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup> In 1613, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a> raiders burned down the settlement, which by then was nominally part of the <a href="/wiki/Johor_Sultanate" title="Johor Sultanate">Johor Sultanate</a> and the island sank into obscurity for the next two centuries,<sup id="cite_ref-country_studies_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-country_studies-17">[16]</a></sup> while the wider maritime region and much trade was under Dutch control.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="British_colonisation_1819.E2.80.931942">British colonisation 1819–1942</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Part_of_Singapore_Island_(British_Library_India_Office_Records,_1825,_detail).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Part_of_Singapore_Island_%28British_Library_India_Office_Records%2C_1825%2C_detail%29.jpg/220px-Part_of_Singapore_Island_%28British_Library_India_Office_Records%2C_1825%2C_detail%29.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Part_of_Singapore_Island_%28British_Library_India_Office_Records%2C_1825%2C_detail%29.jpg/330px-Part_of_Singapore_Island_%28British_Library_India_Office_Records%2C_1825%2C_detail%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Part_of_Singapore_Island_%28British_Library_India_Office_Records%2C_1825%2C_detail%29.jpg/440px-Part_of_Singapore_Island_%28British_Library_India_Office_Records%2C_1825%2C_detail%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3395" data-file-height="2256"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Part_of_Singapore_Island_(British_Library_India_Office_Records,_1825,_detail).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 1825 survey map. Singapore's 
        <a href="/wiki/Free_port" title="Free port" class="mw-redirect">free port</a> trade was centred at 
        <a href="/wiki/Singapore_River" title="Singapore River">Singapore River</a> for 150 years. 
        <a href="/wiki/Fort_Canning" title="Fort Canning">Fort Canning</a> hill was home to its ancient and early colonial rulers.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 1819, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Stamford_Raffles" title="Thomas Stamford Raffles" class="mw-redirect">Thomas Stamford Raffles</a> arrived and signed a treaty with <a href="/wiki/Sultan_Hussein_Shah" title="Sultan Hussein Shah" class="mw-redirect">Sultan Hussein Shah</a> of <a href="/wiki/Johor" title="Johor">Johor</a>, on behalf of the British East India Company, to develop the southern part of Singapore as a <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British</a> trading post. In 1824, the entire island, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Temenggung" title="Temenggung">Temenggong</a>, became a British possession after a further treaty with the Sultan.<sup id="cite_ref-Founding_of_Modern_Singapore_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Founding_of_Modern_Singapore-18">[17]</a></sup> In 1826, Singapore became part of the <a href="/wiki/Straits_Settlements" title="Straits Settlements">Straits Settlements</a>, under the jurisdiction of <a href="/wiki/British_India" title="British India" class="mw-redirect">British India</a>, becoming the regional capital in 1836.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Photographic_Views_of_Singapore_Plate_03_Raffles%27_Square.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Photographic_Views_of_Singapore_Plate_03_Raffles%27_Square.jpg/220px-Photographic_Views_of_Singapore_Plate_03_Raffles%27_Square.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Photographic_Views_of_Singapore_Plate_03_Raffles%27_Square.jpg/330px-Photographic_Views_of_Singapore_Plate_03_Raffles%27_Square.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Photographic_Views_of_Singapore_Plate_03_Raffles%27_Square.jpg/440px-Photographic_Views_of_Singapore_Plate_03_Raffles%27_Square.jpg 2x" data-file-width="898" data-file-height="596"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Photographic_Views_of_Singapore_Plate_03_Raffles%27_Square.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Raffles_Place" title="Raffles Place">Raffles Place</a> c.1900.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Prior to Raffles' arrival, there were only about a thousand people living on the island, mostly <a href="/wiki/Orang_Asal" title="Orang Asal">indigenous Malays</a> along with a handful of <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people" title="Chinese people">Chinese</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Malays_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Malays-20">[19]</a></sup> By 1860, the population had swelled to more than 80,000 and more than half were Chinese. Many immigrants came to work at <a href="/wiki/Rubber" title="Rubber" class="mw-redirect">rubber</a> plantations and, after the 1870s, the island became a global centre for rubber exports.<sup id="cite_ref-Founding_of_Modern_Singapore_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Founding_of_Modern_Singapore-18">[17]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>After the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">First World War</a>, the British built the large <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Naval_Base" title="Singapore Naval Base">Singapore Naval Base</a>. Lieutenant General Sir <a href="/wiki/William_George_Shedden_Dobbie" title="William George Shedden Dobbie" class="mw-redirect">William George Shedden Dobbie</a> was appointed <a href="/wiki/General_Officer_Commanding" title="General Officer Commanding" class="mw-redirect">General Officer Commanding</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Malaya_Command" title="Malaya Command">Malaya Command</a> on 8 November 1935, holding the post until 1939;<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II_and_Japanese_occupation_1942.E2.80.9345">World War II and Japanese occupation 1942–45</span></h3> 
     <p>in May 1938, the <a href="/wiki/General_Officer_Commanding" title="General Officer Commanding" class="mw-redirect">General Officer Commanding</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Malaya_Command" title="Malaya Command">Malaya Command</a> warned how Singapore <a href="/wiki/William_Dobbie#Dobbie.27s_hypothesis_to_the_fall_of_Singapore" title="William Dobbie">could be conquered by the Japanese via an attack from northern Malaya</a>, but his warnings went unheeded.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Japanese_Army" title="Imperial Japanese Army">Imperial Japanese Army</a> invaded <a href="/wiki/British_Malaya" title="British Malaya">British Malaya</a>, culminating in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Singapore" title="Battle of Singapore">Battle of Singapore</a>. When the British surrendered on 15 February 1942, British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> called the defeat "the worst disaster and largest capitulation in British history".<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup> Between 5,000 and 25,000 ethnic Chinese people were killed in the subsequent <a href="/wiki/Sook_Ching_massacre" title="Sook Ching massacre" class="mw-redirect">Sook Ching massacre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>From November 1944 to May 1945, the Allies conducted an intensive <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Singapore_(1944%E2%80%9345)" title="Bombing of Singapore (1944–45)">bombing of Singapore</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Return_of_the_British_1945.E2.80.9359">Return of the British 1945–59</span></h3> 
     <p>After the <a href="/wiki/Surrender_of_Japan" title="Surrender of Japan">surrender of Japan</a> was announced in the <i><a href="/wiki/Jewel_Voice_Broadcast" title="Jewel Voice Broadcast">Jewel Voice Broadcast</a></i> by the Japanese Emperor on 15 August 1945 there was a breakdown of order and looting and revenge-killing were widespread. The formal <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Occupation_of_Singapore" title="Japanese Occupation of Singapore" class="mw-redirect">Japanese Occupation of Singapore</a> was only ended by <a href="/wiki/Operation_Tiderace" title="Operation Tiderace">Operation Tiderace</a><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> and the formal surrender on 12 September 1945 at <a href="/wiki/Singapore_City_Hall" title="Singapore City Hall" class="mw-redirect">Singapore City Hall</a> when Lord <a href="/wiki/Louis_Mountbatten" title="Louis Mountbatten" class="mw-redirect">Louis Mountbatten</a>, Supreme Allied Commander of Southeast Asia Command, accepted the capitulation of Japanese forces in South East Asia from General Itagaki Seishiro.</p> 
     <p>A British Military Administration was then formed to govern the island. On 1 April 1946, the Straits Settlements were dissolved and Singapore became a separate Crown Colony with a civil administration headed by a Governor. Much of the infrastructure had been destroyed during the war, including the harbour, electricity, telephone and water supply systems. There was also a shortage of food leading to malnutrition, disease, and rampant crime and violence. High food prices, unemployment, and workers' discontent culminated into a series of strikes in 1947 causing massive stoppages in public transport and other services. In July 1947, separate Executive and Legislative Councils were established and the election of six members of the Legislative Council was scheduled for the following year. By late 1947, the economy began to recover, facilitated by a growing demand for tin and rubber around the world, but it would take several more years before the economy returned to pre-war levels.</p> 
     <p>The failure of Britain to defend Singapore had destroyed its credibility as an infallible ruler in the eyes of Singaporeans. The decades after the war saw a political awakening amongst the local populace and the rise of anti-colonial and nationalist sentiments, epitomized by the slogan <i>Merdeka</i>, or "independence" in the Malay language.</p> 
     <p>During the 1950s, Chinese Communists with strong ties to the trade unions and Chinese schools carried out armed uprising against the government, leading to the <a href="/wiki/Malayan_Emergency" title="Malayan Emergency">Malayan Emergency</a> and later, the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Insurgency_War" title="Communist Insurgency War">Communist Insurgency War</a>. The <a href="/wiki/1954_National_Service_Riots" title="1954 National Service Riots" class="mw-redirect">1954 National Service Riots</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_middle_schools_riots" title="Chinese middle schools riots">Chinese middle schools riots</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hock_Lee_bus_riots" title="Hock Lee bus riots">Hock Lee bus riots</a> in Singapore were all linked to these events.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/David_Marshall_(Singaporean_politician)" title="David Marshall (Singaporean politician)">David Marshall</a>, pro-independence leader of the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Front" title="Labour Front">Labour Front</a>, won Singapore's first general election in 1955. He led a delegation to London, but Britain rejected his demand for complete self-rule. He resigned and was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Lim_Yew_Hock" title="Lim Yew Hock">Lim Yew Hock</a>, whose policies convinced Britain to grant Singapore full internal <a href="/wiki/Self-governance_of_Singapore" title="Self-governance of Singapore">self-government</a> for all matters except defence and foreign affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Self-government_1959.E2.80.9363">Self-government 1959–63</span></h3> 
     <p>During the <a href="/wiki/Singaporean_general_election,_1959" title="Singaporean general election, 1959">May 1959 elections</a>, the People's Action Party won a landslide victory. Singapore became an internally self-governing state within the Commonwealth, with <a href="/wiki/Lee_Kuan_Yew" title="Lee Kuan Yew">Lee Kuan Yew</a> as its first Prime Minister.<sup id="cite_ref-yewnyt_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yewnyt-30">[29]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Singapore" title="Governor of Singapore" class="mw-redirect">Governor</a> Sir <a href="/wiki/William_Allmond_Codrington_Goode" title="William Allmond Codrington Goode">William Allmond Codrington Goode</a> served as the first <a href="/wiki/Yang_di-Pertuan_Negara" title="Yang di-Pertuan Negara">Yang di-Pertuan Negara</a> (Head of State), and was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Yusof_bin_Ishak" title="Yusof bin Ishak" class="mw-redirect">Yusof bin Ishak</a>, who became the first President of Singapore in 1965.<sup id="cite_ref-Law_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law-31">[30]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Merger_with_Malaysia_1963.E2.80.9365">Merger with Malaysia 1963–65</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Singapore_during_the_formation_of_Malaysia_(16_September_1963).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Singapore_during_the_formation_of_Malaysia_%2816_September_1963%29.jpg/220px-Singapore_during_the_formation_of_Malaysia_%2816_September_1963%29.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Singapore_during_the_formation_of_Malaysia_%2816_September_1963%29.jpg/330px-Singapore_during_the_formation_of_Malaysia_%2816_September_1963%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Singapore_during_the_formation_of_Malaysia_%2816_September_1963%29.jpg/440px-Singapore_during_the_formation_of_Malaysia_%2816_September_1963%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="639" data-file-height="424"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Singapore_during_the_formation_of_Malaysia_(16_September_1963).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The founding father of modern Singapore, 
        <a href="/wiki/Lee_Kuan_Yew" title="Lee Kuan Yew">Lee Kuan Yew</a> declaring the formation of the Federation of Malaysia on 16 September 1963 in Singapore.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>As a result of the <a href="/wiki/1962_Merger_Referendum_of_Singapore" title="1962 Merger Referendum of Singapore" class="mw-redirect">1962 Merger Referendum</a>, on 31 August 1963 Singapore joined with the <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Malaya" title="Federation of Malaya">Federation of Malaya</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Crown_Colony_of_Sarawak" title="Crown Colony of Sarawak">Crown Colony of Sarawak</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Crown_Colony_of_North_Borneo" title="Crown Colony of North Borneo">Crown Colony of North Borneo</a> to form the new federation of Malaysia under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Malaysia_Agreement" title="Malaysia Agreement">Malaysia Agreement</a>. Singaporean leaders chose to join Malaysia primarily due to concerns over its limited land size, scarcity of water, markets and natural resources. Some Singaporean and Malaysian politicians were also concerned that the communists might form the government on the island, a possibility perceived as an external threat to the Federation of Malaya.</p> 
     <p>However, shortly after the merger, the Singapore state government and the Malaysian central government disagreed on many political and economic issues, and communal strife culminated in the <a href="/wiki/1964_race_riots_in_Singapore" title="1964 race riots in Singapore">1964 race riots in Singapore</a>. After many <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Action_Party%E2%80%93United_Malays_National_Organisation_relations" title="People's Action Party–United Malays National Organisation relations">heated ideological conflicts between the two governments</a>, on 9 August 1965, the Malaysian Parliament voted 126 to 0 to expel Singapore from Malaysia with Singaporean delegates not present.<sup id="cite_ref-LOC2_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOC2-9">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_1965.E2.80.93present">Independence 1965–present</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:A_Night_Perspective_on_the_Singapore_Merlion_(8347645113).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/A_Night_Perspective_on_the_Singapore_Merlion_%288347645113%29.jpg/220px-A_Night_Perspective_on_the_Singapore_Merlion_%288347645113%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/A_Night_Perspective_on_the_Singapore_Merlion_%288347645113%29.jpg/330px-A_Night_Perspective_on_the_Singapore_Merlion_%288347645113%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/A_Night_Perspective_on_the_Singapore_Merlion_%288347645113%29.jpg/440px-A_Night_Perspective_on_the_Singapore_Merlion_%288347645113%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1962" data-file-height="1308"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:A_Night_Perspective_on_the_Singapore_Merlion_(8347645113).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> A symbol of Singapore, the 
        <a href="/wiki/Merlion" title="Merlion">Merlion</a> was created in 1964
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Singapore gained independence as the Republic of Singapore (remaining within the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>) on 9 August 1965.<sup id="cite_ref-LOC2_9-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOC2-9">[8]</a></sup> Race riots <a href="/wiki/1969_race_riots_of_Singapore" title="1969 race riots of Singapore">broke out once more</a> in 1969. In 1967, the country co-founded <a href="/wiki/ASEAN" title="ASEAN" class="mw-redirect">ASEAN</a>, the Association of Southeast Asian Nations,<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup> and in 1970 it joined the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>. <a href="/wiki/Lee_Kuan_Yew" title="Lee Kuan Yew">Lee Kuan Yew</a> became Prime Minister, leading its <a href="/wiki/Third_world" title="Third world" class="mw-redirect">Third world</a> economy to <a href="/wiki/First_world" title="First world" class="mw-redirect">First world</a> affluence in a single generation. His emphasis on rapid economic growth, support for business entrepreneurship, limitations on internal democracy, and close relationships with China set the new nation's policies for the next half-century.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lky-7prin_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lky-7prin-36">[35]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 1990, <a href="/wiki/Goh_Chok_Tong" title="Goh Chok Tong">Goh Chok Tong</a> succeeded Lee as Prime Minister, while the latter continued serving in the Cabinet as <a href="/wiki/Senior_Minister" title="Senior Minister">Senior Minister</a> until 2004, and then <a href="/wiki/Minister_Mentor" title="Minister Mentor">Minister Mentor</a> until May 2011. During Goh's tenure, the country faced the <a href="/wiki/1997_Asian_financial_crisis" title="1997 Asian financial crisis">1997 Asian financial crisis</a>, the 2003 <a href="/wiki/Severe_acute_respiratory_syndrome" title="Severe acute respiratory syndrome">SARS</a> outbreak and <a href="/wiki/Terrorist" title="Terrorist" class="mw-redirect">terrorist</a> threats posed by <a href="/wiki/Jemaah_Islamiyah" title="Jemaah Islamiyah">Jemaah Islamiyah</a>.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:View_of_MBS_from_the_gardens_(8026531707).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/View_of_MBS_from_the_gardens_%288026531707%29.jpg/220px-View_of_MBS_from_the_gardens_%288026531707%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/View_of_MBS_from_the_gardens_%288026531707%29.jpg/330px-View_of_MBS_from_the_gardens_%288026531707%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/View_of_MBS_from_the_gardens_%288026531707%29.jpg/440px-View_of_MBS_from_the_gardens_%288026531707%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3455" data-file-height="2303"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:View_of_MBS_from_the_gardens_(8026531707).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Integrated_resort" title="Integrated resort">integrated resort</a> of 
        <a href="/wiki/Marina_Bay_Sands" title="Marina Bay Sands">Marina Bay Sands</a>, that opened in 2010, is one of the world's most photographed buildings. View from 
        <a href="/wiki/Gardens_by_the_Bay" title="Gardens by the Bay">Gardens by the Bay</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 2004, <a href="/wiki/Lee_Hsien_Loong" title="Lee Hsien Loong">Lee Hsien Loong</a>, the eldest son of Lee Kuan Yew, became the country's third Prime Minister. Goh Chok Tong remained in Cabinet as the Senior Minister until May 2011, when he was named Emeritus Senior Minister despite his retirement. He steered the nation through the <a href="/wiki/2008_global_financial_crisis" title="2008 global financial crisis" class="mw-redirect">2008 global financial crisis</a>, resolved the disputed 79-year old <a href="/wiki/Tanjong_Pagar_railway_station" title="Tanjong Pagar railway station">Malayan railways land</a>, and introduced <a href="/wiki/Integrated_resort" title="Integrated resort">integrated resorts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup> Despite the economy's exceptional growth, PAP suffered its <a href="/wiki/Singaporean_general_election,_2011" title="Singaporean general election, 2011">worst election results</a> in 2011, winning 60% of votes, amidst hot-button issues of high influx of foreign workers and cost of living. Lee initiated a major re-structuring of the economy to raise productivity, improved universal healthcare and grants, especially for the pioneer generation of citizens, amongst many new inclusive measures.</p> 
     <p>On 23 March 2015, its founding prime minister, Lee Kuan Yew, who had 'personified Singapore to the world' for nearly half a century died.<sup id="cite_ref-lky-7prin_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lky-7prin-36">[35]</a></sup> In a week of national mourning, 1.7 million residents and guests paid tribute to him at his <a href="/wiki/Lying-in-state" title="Lying-in-state" class="mw-redirect">lying-in-state</a> at <a href="/wiki/Parliament_House,_Singapore" title="Parliament House, Singapore">Parliament House</a> and at community sites around the island.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Singapore celebrated its <a href="/wiki/Golden_jubilee" title="Golden jubilee">Golden jubilee</a> in 2015 – its 50th year of independence, with a year-long series of events branded <b>SG50</b>. The PAP maintained its dominance in Parliament at the <a href="/wiki/GE2015" title="GE2015" class="mw-redirect">September general elections</a>, receiving 69.9% of the popular vote, its second-highest polling result behind the 2001 tally of 75.3%.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Singapore" title="Government of Singapore">Government of Singapore</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Singapore" title="Politics of Singapore">Politics of Singapore</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Singapore" title="Human rights in Singapore">Human rights in Singapore</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Singapore" title="Administrative divisions of Singapore">Administrative divisions of Singapore</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:ParliamentHouse-Singapore-20071120.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/ParliamentHouse-Singapore-20071120.jpg/220px-ParliamentHouse-Singapore-20071120.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/ParliamentHouse-Singapore-20071120.jpg/330px-ParliamentHouse-Singapore-20071120.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/ParliamentHouse-Singapore-20071120.jpg/440px-ParliamentHouse-Singapore-20071120.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:ParliamentHouse-Singapore-20071120.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Singapore's 
        <a href="/wiki/Parliament_House,_Singapore" title="Parliament House, Singapore">Parliament House</a>, beside the 
        <a href="/wiki/Singapore_River" title="Singapore River">Singapore River</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Singapore is a parliamentary republic with a <a href="/wiki/Westminster_system" title="Westminster system">Westminster system</a> of unicameral parliamentary government representing <a href="/wiki/Constituencies_of_Singapore" title="Constituencies of Singapore">constituencies</a>. The country's <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Singapore" title="Constitution of Singapore">constitution</a> establishes a <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy_in_Singapore" title="Representative democracy in Singapore">representative democracy</a> as the political system.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated4_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated4-39">[38]</a></sup> Executive power rests with the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Singapore" title="Cabinet of Singapore">Cabinet of Singapore</a>, led by the Prime Minister and, to a much lesser extent, the President.<sup id="cite_ref-Law_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law-31">[30]</a></sup> The President is elected through a popular vote, and has <a href="/wiki/Veto" title="Veto">veto</a> powers over a specific set of executive decisions, such as the use of the national reserves and the appointment of judges, but otherwise occupies a largely ceremonial post.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Parliament serves as the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_branch" title="Legislative branch" class="mw-redirect">legislative branch</a> of the government.<sup id="cite_ref-Law_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law-31">[30]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Members_of_Parliament" title="Members of Parliament" class="mw-redirect">Members of Parliament</a> (MPs) consist of elected, non-constituency and nominated members. Elected MPs are voted into the Parliament on a "<a href="/wiki/First-past-the-post_voting" title="First-past-the-post voting">first-past-the-post</a>" (plurality) basis and represent either single-member or <a href="/wiki/Group_representation_constituencies" title="Group representation constituencies" class="mw-redirect">group representation constituencies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-parliament.gov.sg_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parliament.gov.sg-41">[40]</a></sup> The People's Action Party has won control of Parliament with large majorities in every election since self-governance was secured in 1959.<sup id="cite_ref-freedomhouse_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedomhouse-42">[41]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Although the elections are clean, there is no independent electoral authority and the government has strong influence on the media. <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> ranks Singapore as "partly free" in its <i><a href="/wiki/Freedom_in_the_World" title="Freedom in the World">Freedom in the World</a></i> report,<sup id="cite_ref-freedomhouse_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedomhouse-42">[41]</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i> ranks Singapore as a "flawed democracy", the second best rank of four, in its "<a href="/wiki/Democracy_Index" title="Democracy Index">Democracy Index</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> Despite this, in the 2011 Parliamentary elections, the opposition, led by the <a href="/wiki/Workers%27_Party_of_Singapore" title="Workers' Party of Singapore" class="mw-redirect">Workers' Party</a>, increased its representation to seven elected MPs.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup> In the 2015 elections, PAP scored a landslide victory, winning 83 of 89 seats contested, with 70% of popular votes. <a href="/wiki/Gallup_(company)" title="Gallup (company)">Gallup</a> polls reported 84% of residents in Singapore expressed confidence in the government, and 85% in its judicial systems and courts – one of the highest ratings in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Singapore's governance model eschews <a href="/wiki/Populist" title="Populist" class="mw-redirect">populist</a> politics, focusing on the nation's long-term interest, and is known to be clean, effective and pragmatic. As a small nation highly dependent on external trade, it is vulnerable to geo-politics and global economics. It places great emphasis on security and stability of the region in its foreign policies, and applies global best practices to ensure the nation's attractiveness as an investment destination and business hub.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lky-7prin_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lky-7prin-36">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sg-unicorn_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sg-unicorn-48">[47]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Supreme_Court_of_Singapore_at_night_(HDR)_-_20071115.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Supreme_Court_of_Singapore_at_night_%28HDR%29_-_20071115.jpg/220px-Supreme_Court_of_Singapore_at_night_%28HDR%29_-_20071115.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Supreme_Court_of_Singapore_at_night_%28HDR%29_-_20071115.jpg/330px-Supreme_Court_of_Singapore_at_night_%28HDR%29_-_20071115.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Supreme_Court_of_Singapore_at_night_%28HDR%29_-_20071115.jpg/440px-Supreme_Court_of_Singapore_at_night_%28HDR%29_-_20071115.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2600"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Supreme_Court_of_Singapore_at_night_(HDR)_-_20071115.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> New and old 
        <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Singapore" title="Supreme Court of Singapore">Supreme Court</a> buildings. The 
        <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Appeal" title="Court of Appeal" class="mw-redirect">Court of Appeal</a> occupies the 'disc' atop, representing the highest level of 
        <a href="/wiki/Justice" title="Justice">justice</a>, and a modern interpretation of the 
        <a href="/wiki/Dome" title="Dome">dome</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Singapore" title="Law of Singapore">legal system of Singapore</a> is based on <a href="/wiki/English_common_law" title="English common law" class="mw-redirect">English common law</a>, but with substantial local differences. <a href="/wiki/Trial_by_jury" title="Trial by jury" class="mw-redirect">Trial by jury</a> was abolished in 1970 so that judicial decisions would rest entirely in the hands of appointed judges.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> Singapore has penalties that include <a href="/wiki/Judicial_corporal_punishment" title="Judicial corporal punishment">judicial corporal punishment</a> in the form of <a href="/wiki/Caning_in_Singapore" title="Caning in Singapore">caning</a>, which may be imposed for such offences as rape, rioting, vandalism, and certain immigration offences.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup> There is a mandatory <a href="/wiki/Capital_punishment_in_Singapore" title="Capital punishment in Singapore">death penalty</a> for murder, as well as for certain aggravated drug-trafficking and firearms offences.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> has said that some legal provisions of the Singapore system conflict with the right to be presumed innocent until proven guilty, and that Singapore has "... possibly the highest execution rate in the world relative to its population".<sup id="cite_ref-amnesty_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amnesty-53">[52]</a></sup> The government has disputed Amnesty's claims.<sup id="cite_ref-response_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-response-54">[53]</a></sup> In a 2008 survey of international business executives, Singapore received the top ranking with regard to judicial system quality in Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup> Singapore has been consistently rated among the least corrupt countries in the world by <a href="/wiki/Transparency_International" title="Transparency International">Transparency International</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2011, the <a href="/wiki/World_Justice_Project" title="World Justice Project">World Justice Project</a>'s <i>Rule of Law Index</i> ranked Singapore among the top countries surveyed with regard to "order and security", "absence of corruption", and "effective criminal justice". However, the country received a much lower ranking for "<a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_speech" title="Freedom of speech">freedom of speech</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_assembly" title="Freedom of assembly">freedom of assembly</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup> All public gatherings of five or more people require police permits, and protests may legally be held only at the <a href="/wiki/Speakers%27_Corner,_Singapore" title="Speakers' Corner, Singapore">Speakers' Corner</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Singapore" title="Foreign relations of Singapore">Foreign relations of Singapore</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Lee_Kuan_Yew_Cohen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Ambassador to the USA Chan Heng Chee, Lee Kuan Yew, and US Secretary of Defense William Cohen in a room" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Lee_Kuan_Yew_Cohen.jpg/220px-Lee_Kuan_Yew_Cohen.jpg" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Lee_Kuan_Yew_Cohen.jpg/330px-Lee_Kuan_Yew_Cohen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Lee_Kuan_Yew_Cohen.jpg/440px-Lee_Kuan_Yew_Cohen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2670" data-file-height="1970"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Lee_Kuan_Yew_Cohen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Then 
        <a href="/wiki/Senior_Minister" title="Senior Minister">Senior Minister</a> Lee Kuan Yew and Ambassador to the US 
        <a href="/wiki/Chan_Heng_Chee" title="Chan Heng Chee">Chan Heng Chee</a>, met with US Secretary of Defense 
        <a href="/wiki/William_Cohen" title="William Cohen">William Cohen</a> during a visit in 2000.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Singapore's foreign policy is aimed at maintaining security in Southeast Asia and surrounding territories. An underlying principle is political and economic stability in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-govt.nz_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-govt.nz-59">[58]</a></sup> It has diplomatic relations with more than 180 sovereign states.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup> Since 2002, it has hosted the annual inter-government security forum <a href="/wiki/Shangri-La_Dialogue" title="Shangri-La Dialogue">Shangri-La Dialogue</a>, by the <a href="/wiki/International_Institute_for_Strategic_Studies" title="International Institute for Strategic Studies">International Institute for Strategic Studies</a>, attended by ministers and defence officials from the Asia-Pacific and Europe. The high-level dialogue has had influence on confrontational issues, such as territorial disputes in the East and South China seas, together with discussions about global security and terrorism.</p> 
     <p>As one of the five founding members of ASEAN,<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup> it is a strong supporter of the <a href="/wiki/ASEAN_Free_Trade_Area" title="ASEAN Free Trade Area">ASEAN Free Trade Area</a> (AFTA) and the ASEAN Investment Area, because Singapore's economy is closely linked to that of the region as a whole. Former Prime Minister Goh Chok Tong proposed the formation of an <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Southeast_Asian_Nations#Economic_community" title="Association of Southeast Asian Nations">ASEAN Economic Community</a>, a step beyond the current AFTA, bringing it closer to a <a href="/wiki/Common_market" title="Common market" class="mw-redirect">common market</a>. This was agreed to in 2007 for implementation by 2015. Other regional organisations are important to Singapore, and it is the host of the APEC Secretariat. Singapore maintains membership in other regional organisations, such as <a href="/wiki/Asia%E2%80%93Europe_Meeting" title="Asia–Europe Meeting" class="mw-redirect">Asia–Europe Meeting</a>, the Forum for East Asia-Latin American Cooperation, the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Network_of_Major_Cities_21" title="Asian Network of Major Cities 21">Asian Network of Major Cities 21</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/East_Asia_Summit" title="East Asia Summit">East Asia Summit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-govt.nz_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-govt.nz-59">[58]</a></sup> It is also a member of the Non-Aligned Movement<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup> and the Commonwealth.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Barack_Obama_at_ASEAN_Summit_2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Barack Obama attends the Trans-Pacific Partnership (TPP) meeting at ASEAN Summit 2012" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Barack_Obama_at_ASEAN_Summit_2012.jpg/220px-Barack_Obama_at_ASEAN_Summit_2012.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Barack_Obama_at_ASEAN_Summit_2012.jpg/330px-Barack_Obama_at_ASEAN_Summit_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Barack_Obama_at_ASEAN_Summit_2012.jpg/440px-Barack_Obama_at_ASEAN_Summit_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4096" data-file-height="2731"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Barack_Obama_at_ASEAN_Summit_2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Prime Minister 
        <a href="/wiki/Lee_Hsien_Loong" title="Lee Hsien Loong">Lee Hsien Loong</a> and US President 
        <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> attended the 
        <a href="/wiki/Trans-Pacific_Partnership" title="Trans-Pacific Partnership">Trans-Pacific Partnership</a> (TPP) meeting at 
        <a href="/wiki/ASEAN_Summit" title="ASEAN Summit">ASEAN Summit</a> 2012.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In general, bilateral relations with other ASEAN members are strong; however, disagreements have arisen,<sup id="cite_ref-govt.nz_59-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-govt.nz-59">[58]</a></sup> and relations with neighbouring Malaysia and <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> have sometimes been strained.<sup id="cite_ref-Rocky_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rocky-64">[63]</a></sup> Malaysia and Singapore have clashed over the delivery of <a href="/wiki/Fresh_water" title="Fresh water">fresh water</a> to Singapore,<sup id="cite_ref-Disputes_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Disputes-65">[64]</a></sup> and access by the Singapore Armed Forces to Malaysian airspace.<sup id="cite_ref-Rocky_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rocky-64">[63]</a></sup> Border issues exist with Malaysia and Indonesia, and both have banned the sale of marine sand to Singapore over disputes about Singapore's land reclamation.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup> Some previous disputes have been resolved by the <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a>. Piracy in the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Malacca" title="Strait of Malacca">Strait of Malacca</a> has been a cause of concern for all three countries.<sup id="cite_ref-Disputes_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Disputes-65">[64]</a></sup> Close economic ties exist with <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a>, and the two share a pegged currency value.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The first diplomatic contact with <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> was made in the 1970s, with full diplomatic relations established in the 1990s. Since then the two countries have been major players in strengthening the ASEAN–China relationship.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup> Singapore and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> share a long-standing close relationship, in particular in defence, the economy, health, and education. The United States was Singapore's third largest trading partner in 2010, behind <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> (2nd) and Malaysia (1st).<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> The two countries have a free-trade agreement, and Singapore views its relationship with the United States as an important counterbalance to China's influence.<sup id="cite_ref-diplomat20120214_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diplomat20120214-70">[69]</a></sup> A Strategic Framework Agreement between the two, signed in 2005, formalises security and defence co-operation.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup> Singapore has pushed regional counter-terrorism initiatives, with a strong resolve to deal with terrorists inside its borders. To this end it has given support to the US-led coalition to fight terrorism, with bilateral co-operation in counter-terrorism and counter-proliferation initiatives, and joint military exercises.<sup id="cite_ref-govt.nz_59-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-govt.nz-59">[58]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Armed_Forces" title="Singapore Armed Forces">Singapore Armed Forces</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The Singaporean military is arguably the most technologically advanced in Southeast Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup> It comprises the <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Army" title="Singapore Army">Singapore Army</a>, <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Singapore_Navy" title="Republic of Singapore Navy">Republic of Singapore Navy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Singapore_Air_Force" title="Republic of Singapore Air Force">Republic of Singapore Air Force</a>. It is seen as the guarantor of the country's independence.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup> The nation's philosophy of defence is one of diplomacy and deterrence.<sup id="cite_ref-Mindef18Feb2008_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mindef18Feb2008-74">[73]</a></sup> This principle translates into the culture, involving all citizens in the country's defence.<sup id="cite_ref-MindefApr2005_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MindefApr2005-75">[74]</a></sup> The government spends 4.9% of the country's GDP on the military, and one out of every four dollars of government spending is spent on defence.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_F-15SG_Strike_Eagle,_Singapore_-_Air_Force_JP7096555.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Boeing_F-15SG_Strike_Eagle%2C_Singapore_-_Air_Force_JP7096555.jpg/220px-Boeing_F-15SG_Strike_Eagle%2C_Singapore_-_Air_Force_JP7096555.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Boeing_F-15SG_Strike_Eagle%2C_Singapore_-_Air_Force_JP7096555.jpg/330px-Boeing_F-15SG_Strike_Eagle%2C_Singapore_-_Air_Force_JP7096555.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Boeing_F-15SG_Strike_Eagle%2C_Singapore_-_Air_Force_JP7096555.jpg/440px-Boeing_F-15SG_Strike_Eagle%2C_Singapore_-_Air_Force_JP7096555.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1068"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_F-15SG_Strike_Eagle,_Singapore_-_Air_Force_JP7096555.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Air_Force" title="Singapore Air Force" class="mw-redirect">Singapore Air Force</a>'s 
        <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_F-15E_Strike_Eagle#F-15SG" title="McDonnell Douglas F-15E Strike Eagle">F-15SG</a> are 
        <i><a href="/wiki/Strike_Eagle" title="Strike Eagle" class="mw-redirect">Strike Eagle</a></i> variants (24 units). Pilots also train in 
        <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, 
        <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> and 
        <a href="/wiki/USA" title="USA" class="mw-redirect">USA</a> due to severe airspace constraints.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>After its independence, Singapore had two <a href="/wiki/Infantry" title="Infantry">infantry</a> regiments commanded by British officers. This force was considered too small to provide effective security for the new country, so development of its military forces became a priority.<sup id="cite_ref-cs.uwec_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs.uwec-77">[76]</a></sup> Britain pulled its military out of Singapore in October 1971, leaving behind only a small British, Australian and New Zealand force as a token military presence. The last British soldier left Singapore in March 1976. New Zealand troops were the last to leave, in 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>A great deal of initial support came from <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-cs.uwec_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs.uwec-77">[76]</a></sup> a country that is not recognised by the neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Islamic" title="Islamic" class="mw-redirect">Muslim-majority</a> nations of Malaysia, Indonesia, or Brunei.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup> The main fear after independence was an invasion by Malaysia. <a href="/wiki/Israel_Defense_Forces" title="Israel Defense Forces">Israeli Defense Force</a> (IDF) commanders were tasked with creating the Singapore Armed Forces (SAF) from scratch, and Israeli instructors were brought in to train Singaporean soldiers. Military courses were conducted according to the IDF's format, and Singapore adopted a system of conscription and reserve service based on <a href="/wiki/Conscription_in_Israel" title="Conscription in Israel">the Israeli</a> model.<sup id="cite_ref-cs.uwec_77-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs.uwec-77">[76]</a></sup> Singapore still maintains strong security ties with Israel and is one of the biggest buyers of Israeli arms and weapons systems.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/MATADOR_(weapon)" title="MATADOR (weapon)" class="mw-redirect">MATADOR</a> is one example of recent Singaporean–Israeli collaboration.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The SAF is being developed to respond to a wide range of issues, in both conventional and unconventional warfare. The <a href="/wiki/Defence_Science_and_Technology_Agency" title="Defence Science and Technology Agency">Defence Science and Technology Agency</a> is responsible for procuring resources for the military.<sup id="cite_ref-Mindef18Feb2008_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mindef18Feb2008-74">[73]</a></sup> The geographic restrictions of Singapore mean that the SAF must plan to fully repulse an attack, as they can not fall back and re-group. The small size of the population has also affected the way the SAF has been designed, with a small active force but a large number of reserves.<sup id="cite_ref-MindefApr2005_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MindefApr2005-75">[74]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Singapore has <a href="/wiki/Conscription_in_Singapore" title="Conscription in Singapore" class="mw-redirect">conscription</a> for all able-bodied males at age 18, except those with a criminal record or who can prove that their loss would bring hardship to their families. Males who have yet to complete pre-university education or are awarded the <a href="/wiki/Public_Service_Commission_(Singapore)" title="Public Service Commission (Singapore)">Public Service Commission</a> scholarship can opt to defer their draft. Though not required to perform military service, the number of women in the SAF has been increasing: since 1989 they have been allowed to fill military vocations formerly reserved for men. Before induction into a specific branch of the armed forces, recruits undergo at least 9 weeks of basic military training.<sup id="cite_ref-country-data_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-country-data-84">[83]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_100716-N-0995C-155_The_Singapore_navy_guided-missile_frigate_RSS_Steadfast_(FFG_70)_and_the_corvette_RSS_Vigilance_(90)_are_underway_during_Cooperation_Afloat_Readiness_and_Training_(CARAT)_Singapore_2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/US_Navy_100716-N-0995C-155_The_Singapore_navy_guided-missile_frigate_RSS_Steadfast_%28FFG_70%29_and_the_corvette_RSS_Vigilance_%2890%29_are_underway_during_Cooperation_Afloat_Readiness_and_Training_%28CARAT%29_Singapore_2010.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/US_Navy_100716-N-0995C-155_The_Singapore_navy_guided-missile_frigate_RSS_Steadfast_%28FFG_70%29_and_the_corvette_RSS_Vigilance_%2890%29_are_underway_during_Cooperation_Afloat_Readiness_and_Training_%28CARAT%29_Singapore_2010.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/US_Navy_100716-N-0995C-155_The_Singapore_navy_guided-missile_frigate_RSS_Steadfast_%28FFG_70%29_and_the_corvette_RSS_Vigilance_%2890%29_are_underway_during_Cooperation_Afloat_Readiness_and_Training_%28CARAT%29_Singapore_2010.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1500"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_100716-N-0995C-155_The_Singapore_navy_guided-missile_frigate_RSS_Steadfast_(FFG_70)_and_the_corvette_RSS_Vigilance_(90)_are_underway_during_Cooperation_Afloat_Readiness_and_Training_(CARAT)_Singapore_2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Republic of Singapore Navy's 
        <a href="/wiki/Formidable_class_frigate" title="Formidable class frigate" class="mw-redirect">RSS <i>Steadfast</i></a> and 
        <a href="/wiki/Victory_class_corvette" title="Victory class corvette" class="mw-redirect">RSS <i>Vigilance</i></a> sailing line-abreast during 
        <a href="/wiki/Cooperation_Afloat_Readiness_and_Training" title="Cooperation Afloat Readiness and Training">CARAT Singapore 2010</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Because of the scarcity of open land on the main island, training involving activities such as live firing and <a href="/wiki/Amphibious_warfare" title="Amphibious warfare">amphibious warfare</a> is often carried out on smaller islands, typically barred to civilian access. This also avoids risk to the main island and the city. However, large-scale drills are considered too dangerous to be performed in the area, and since 1975 have been performed in Taiwan.<sup id="cite_ref-country-data_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-country-data-84">[83]</a></sup> Training is also held in about a dozen other countries. In general, military exercises are held with foreign forces once or twice per week.<sup id="cite_ref-MindefApr2005_75-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MindefApr2005-75">[74]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Due to airspace and land constraints, the Republic of Singapore Air Force (RSAF) maintains a number of overseas bases in <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, the United States, and France. The RSAF's 130 Squadron is based in <a href="/wiki/RAAF_Base_Pearce" title="RAAF Base Pearce">RAAF Base Pearce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Western_Australia" title="Western Australia">Western Australia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup> and its <a href="/wiki/126_Squadron,_Republic_of_Singapore_Air_Force" title="126 Squadron, Republic of Singapore Air Force">126 Squadron</a> is based in the <a href="/wiki/Oakey_Army_Aviation_Centre" title="Oakey Army Aviation Centre">Oakey Army Aviation Centre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queensland" title="Queensland">Queensland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup> The RSAF has one squadron—the 150 Squadron—based in <a href="/wiki/Cazaux" title="Cazaux">Cazaux</a> Air Base in southern <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> The RSAF also has a few overseas detachments in the United States, in <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">San Diego</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marana,_Arizona" title="Marana, Arizona">Marana, Arizona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grand_Prairie,_Texas" title="Grand Prairie, Texas">Grand Prairie, Texas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luke_Air_Force_Base" title="Luke Air Force Base">Luke Air Force Base</a>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The SAF has sent forces to assist in operations outside the country, in areas such as <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup> in both military and civilian roles. In the region, it has helped stabilise <a href="/wiki/East_Timor" title="East Timor">East Timor</a> and has provided aid to <a href="/wiki/Aceh" title="Aceh">Aceh</a> in Indonesia following the <a href="/wiki/2004_Indian_Ocean_earthquake_and_tsunami" title="2004 Indian Ocean earthquake and tsunami">2004 Indian Ocean earthquake and tsunami</a>. In 2014, the RSN deployed two ships, the RSS <i>Resolute</i> and the <i>Tenacious</i> to the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Aden" title="Gulf of Aden">Gulf of Aden</a> to aid in counter <a href="/wiki/Piracy" title="Piracy">piracy</a> efforts as part of <a href="/wiki/Combined_Task_Force_151" title="Combined Task Force 151">Task Force 151</a>. The SAF also helped in relief efforts during <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Haiyan" title="Typhoon Haiyan">Typhoon Haiyan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup> Singapore is part of the <a href="/wiki/Five_Power_Defence_Arrangements" title="Five Power Defence Arrangements">Five Power Defence Arrangements</a>, a military alliance with Australia, Malaysia, New Zealand, and the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-MindefApr2005_75-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MindefApr2005-75">[74]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Singapore" title="Geography of Singapore">Geography of Singapore</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:CIA_World_Factbook_map_of_Singapore_(English).png" class="image"><img alt="Map showing Singapore island and the territories belonging to Singapore and its neighbours" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/CIA_World_Factbook_map_of_Singapore_%28English%29.png/220px-CIA_World_Factbook_map_of_Singapore_%28English%29.png" width="220" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/07/CIA_World_Factbook_map_of_Singapore_%28English%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/07/CIA_World_Factbook_map_of_Singapore_%28English%29.png 2x" data-file-width="327" data-file-height="350"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:CIA_World_Factbook_map_of_Singapore_(English).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Outline of Singapore and the surrounding islands and waterways
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Singapore consists of <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_Singapore" title="List of islands of Singapore">63 islands</a>, including the main island, <a href="/wiki/Pulau_Ujong" title="Pulau Ujong">Pulau Ujong</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> There are two man-made connections to Johor, Malaysia: the <a href="/wiki/Johor%E2%80%93Singapore_Causeway" title="Johor–Singapore Causeway">Johor–Singapore Causeway</a> in the north and the <a href="/wiki/Malaysia%E2%80%93Singapore_Second_Link" title="Malaysia–Singapore Second Link">Tuas Second Link</a> in the west. <a href="/wiki/Jurong_Island" title="Jurong Island">Jurong Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pulau_Tekong" title="Pulau Tekong">Pulau Tekong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pulau_Ubin" title="Pulau Ubin">Pulau Ubin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sentosa" title="Sentosa">Sentosa</a> are the largest of Singapore's smaller islands. The highest natural point is <a href="/wiki/Bukit_Timah_Hill" title="Bukit Timah Hill">Bukit Timah Hill</a> at 163.63&nbsp;m (537&nbsp;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Ongoing <a href="/wiki/Land_reclamation" title="Land reclamation">land reclamation</a> projects have increased Singapore's land area from 581.5&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (224.5&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) in the 1960s to 719.1&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (277.6&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) in 2015, an increase of some 23% (130&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-singstat2015pop.26land_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singstat2015pop.26land-10">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup> The country is projected to grow by another 100&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (40&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) by 2030.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup> Some projects involve merging smaller islands through land reclamation to form larger, more functional islands, as has been done with Jurong Island.<sup id="cite_ref-earthshots.usgs.gov_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earthshots.usgs.gov-98">[97]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Singapore_Botanic_Gardens_Palm_Valley.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Singapore_Botanic_Gardens_Palm_Valley.jpg/220px-Singapore_Botanic_Gardens_Palm_Valley.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Singapore_Botanic_Gardens_Palm_Valley.jpg/330px-Singapore_Botanic_Gardens_Palm_Valley.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Singapore_Botanic_Gardens_Palm_Valley.jpg/440px-Singapore_Botanic_Gardens_Palm_Valley.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Singapore_Botanic_Gardens_Palm_Valley.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Botanic_Gardens" title="Singapore Botanic Gardens">Singapore Botanic Gardens</a> is the only 
        <a href="/wiki/Tropical_garden" title="Tropical garden">tropical garden</a> to be inscribed by 
        <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> as a 
        <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Nearly 10% of Singapore's land has been set aside for parks and <a href="/wiki/Nature_reserve" title="Nature reserve">nature reserves</a>. The network of nature reserves, parks, <a href="/wiki/Park_connector" title="Park connector" class="mw-redirect">park connectors</a>, nature ways, tree-lined roads and other natural areas have enhanced the sense of green space in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> This is a result of five decades of greening efforts, which began in 1963, when Prime Minister Lee Kuan Yew launched Singapore's first tree-planting campaign by planting a mempat tree (<i><a href="/wiki/Cratoxylum_formosum" title="Cratoxylum formosum">Cratoxylum formosum</a></i>). The aim was to soften the harshness of urbanisation and improve the quality of life.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup> This initiative continued into the 1970s and 1980s under the Parks and Recreation Department (PRD), renamed the <a href="/wiki/National_Parks_Board" title="National Parks Board">National Parks Board</a> (<a href="/wiki/Abbreviation" title="Abbreviation">abbreviation</a>: NParks) in July 1996.</p> 
     <p>Due to these efforts, Singapore was ranked fourth in the 2014 <a href="/wiki/Environmental_Performance_Index" title="Environmental Performance Index">Environmental Performance Index</a>, which measures the effectiveness of state policies for environmental sustainability.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3> 
     <p>Singapore has a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest_climate" title="Tropical rainforest climate">tropical rainforest climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen</a>: <i>Af</i> ) with no distinctive seasons, uniform temperature and pressure, high humidity, and abundant rainfall. Temperatures usually range from 22 to 35&nbsp;°C (72 to 95&nbsp;°F). <a href="/wiki/Relative_humidity" title="Relative humidity">Relative humidity</a> averages around 79% in the morning and 73% in the afternoon.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (April 2015)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup> April and May are the hottest months, with the wetter <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">monsoon</a> season from November to January.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup> From July to October, there is often <a href="/wiki/Haze" title="Haze">haze</a> caused by <a href="/wiki/Bush_fire" title="Bush fire" class="mw-redirect">bush fires</a> in neighbouring Indonesia, usually from the island of Sumatra.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup> Although Singapore does not observe <a href="/wiki/Daylight_saving_time" title="Daylight saving time">daylight saving time</a> (DST), it follows the GMT+8 time zone, one hour ahead of the typical zone for its geographical location.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[104]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><br></p>
