     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Singapore" title="Economy of Singapore">Economy of Singapore</a>
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-independence_economy">Pre-independence economy</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:RafflesHotel-Singapore-20041025.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/RafflesHotel-Singapore-20041025.jpg/220px-RafflesHotel-Singapore-20041025.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/RafflesHotel-Singapore-20041025.jpg/330px-RafflesHotel-Singapore-20041025.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/RafflesHotel-Singapore-20041025.jpg/440px-RafflesHotel-Singapore-20041025.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1296" data-file-height="972"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:RafflesHotel-Singapore-20041025.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Raffles_Hotel" title="Raffles Hotel">Raffles Hotel</a> (1887), a heritage landmark. The 
        <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Sling" title="Singapore Sling">Singapore Sling</a> cocktail was created at its 
        <i>Long Bar</i>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Before independence in 1965, Singapore was the capital of the British Straits Settlements, a <a href="/wiki/Crown_Colony" title="Crown Colony" class="mw-redirect">Crown Colony</a>. Because it held the main <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Naval_Base" title="Singapore Naval Base">British naval base</a> in East Asia and the largest dry dock of its time, Singapore was commonly described in the press as the '<a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> of the East'.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup> The opening of the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a> in 1869 led to a major increase in trade between Europe and Asia, helping Singapore become a major world trade centre, and the Port of Singapore became the largest and busiest ports in the world from the 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup> Prior to 1965, Singapore had a <a href="/wiki/GDP_per_capita" title="GDP per capita" class="mw-redirect">GDP per capita</a> of $511.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup> After independence, the combination of <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_received_FDI" title="List of countries by received FDI">foreign direct investment</a> and a state-led drive for industrialisation, based on plans by <a href="/wiki/Goh_Keng_Swee" title="Goh Keng Swee">Goh Keng Swee</a> and <a href="/wiki/Albert_Winsemius" title="Albert Winsemius">Albert Winsemius</a>, started the expansion of the country's economy.<sup id="cite_ref-murphy_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-murphy-112">[111]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern-day_economy">Modern-day economy</span></h3> 
     <p>Singapore has a highly developed <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a>, based historically on extended <a href="/wiki/Entrep%C3%B4t" title="Entrepôt">entrepôt</a> trade. Along with <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, Singapore is one of the original Four Asian Tigers, but has surpassed its peers in terms of GDP per capita. The Singaporean economy is known as one of the freest,<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup> most innovative,<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup> most competitive,<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup> most dynamic<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup> and most business-friendly.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Index_of_Economic_Freedom#2015" title="Index of Economic Freedom">2015 Index of Economic Freedom</a> ranks Singapore as the second freest economy in the world. According to the <a href="/wiki/Corruption_Perceptions_Index" title="Corruption Perceptions Index">Corruption Perceptions Index</a>, Singapore is consistently ranked as one of the least corrupt countries in the world, along with <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavian</a> countries.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Singapore_Airlines,_Airbus_A380-800_9V-SKI_%2750th_anniversary_of_Singapore%27_NRT_(20786371995).jpg" class="image"><img alt="Singapore Airlines celebrated the nation's Golden Jubilee with its Airbus A380 in SG50 livery" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Singapore_Airlines%2C_Airbus_A380-800_9V-SKI_%2750th_anniversary_of_Singapore%27_NRT_%2820786371995%29.jpg/220px-Singapore_Airlines%2C_Airbus_A380-800_9V-SKI_%2750th_anniversary_of_Singapore%27_NRT_%2820786371995%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Singapore_Airlines%2C_Airbus_A380-800_9V-SKI_%2750th_anniversary_of_Singapore%27_NRT_%2820786371995%29.jpg/330px-Singapore_Airlines%2C_Airbus_A380-800_9V-SKI_%2750th_anniversary_of_Singapore%27_NRT_%2820786371995%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Singapore_Airlines%2C_Airbus_A380-800_9V-SKI_%2750th_anniversary_of_Singapore%27_NRT_%2820786371995%29.jpg/440px-Singapore_Airlines%2C_Airbus_A380-800_9V-SKI_%2750th_anniversary_of_Singapore%27_NRT_%2820786371995%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3877" data-file-height="2590"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Singapore_Airlines,_Airbus_A380-800_9V-SKI_%2750th_anniversary_of_Singapore%27_NRT_(20786371995).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Airlines" title="Singapore Airlines">Singapore Airlines</a> celebrated 
        <a href="/wiki/Golden_Jubilee" title="Golden Jubilee" class="mw-redirect">Golden Jubilee</a> with its 
        <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a> in 'SG50' 
        <a href="/wiki/Livery" title="Livery">livery</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>For the past decade, Singapore has been the only Asian country to receive the top-tier AAA sovereign <a href="/wiki/Credit_rating" title="Credit rating">ratings</a> from all major <a href="/wiki/Credit_rating_agencies" title="Credit rating agencies" class="mw-redirect">credit rating agencies</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Standard_%26_Poor%27s" title="Standard &amp; Poor's">Standard &amp; Poor's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moody%27s" title="Moody's" class="mw-redirect">Moody's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fitch_Ratings" title="Fitch Ratings">Fitch</a>. Globally, it is one of only nine countries with AAA rating from the <a href="/wiki/Big_Three_(credit_rating_agencies)" title="Big Three (credit rating agencies)">Big Three (credit rating agencies)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup> Singapore attracts a large amount of foreign investment as a result of its location, skilled workforce, low tax rates, advanced <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure" title="Infrastructure">infrastructure</a> and zero-tolerance against corruption.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup> There are more than 7,000 multinational corporations from the United States, Japan, and Europe in Singapore. There are also approximately 1,500 companies from China and a similar number from India. Foreign firms are found in almost all sectors of the country's economy. Singapore is also the second-largest foreign investor in India.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup> Roughly 44 percent of the Singaporean workforce is made up of non-Singaporeans.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup> Over ten <a href="/wiki/Free-trade_agreement" title="Free-trade agreement" class="mw-redirect">free-trade agreements</a> have been signed with other countries and regions.<sup id="cite_ref-govt.nz_59-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-govt.nz-59">[58]</a></sup> Despite market freedom, Singapore's government operations have a significant stake in the economy, contributing 22% of the GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Singapore is considered a barometer of global economic health, especially within Asia, owing to its high dependence on external trade. Its foreign trade and capital flows is 407.9% of its GDP, making it the most trade dependent country in the world. It is the 14th largest exporter and the 15th largest importer in the world.</p> 
     <dl> 
      <dd>

     </dl> 
     <p>Singapore has the world's eleventh <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_foreign_exchange_reserves" title="List of countries by foreign exchange reserves" class="mw-redirect">largest foreign reserves</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup> and one of the highest <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_net_international_investment_position_per_capita" title="List of countries by net international investment position per capita">net international investment position per capita</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The currency of Singapore is the <a href="/wiki/Singapore_dollar" title="Singapore dollar">Singapore dollar</a> (SGD or S$), issued by the <a href="/wiki/Monetary_Authority_of_Singapore" title="Monetary Authority of Singapore">Monetary Authority of Singapore</a> (MAS).<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup> It is interchangeable with the <a href="/wiki/Brunei_dollar" title="Brunei dollar">Brunei dollar</a> at <a href="/wiki/Par_value" title="Par value">par value</a> since 1967, owing to their historically close relations.<sup id="cite_ref-Currency_History_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Currency_History-137">[136]</a></sup> MAS manages its <a href="/wiki/Monetary_policy" title="Monetary policy">monetary policy</a> by allowing the Singapore dollar <a href="/wiki/Exchange_rate" title="Exchange rate">exchange rate</a> to rise or fall within an undisclosed trading band. This is different from most <a href="/wiki/Central_banks" title="Central banks" class="mw-redirect">central banks</a>, which use <a href="/wiki/Interest_rates" title="Interest rates" class="mw-redirect">interest rates</a> to manage policy.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup> In recent years, the country has been identified as an increasingly popular <a href="/wiki/Tax_haven" title="Tax haven">tax haven</a> for the wealthy due to the low tax rate on personal income and tax exemptions on foreign-based income and capital gains. Australian millionaire retailer Brett Blundy and multi-billionaire Facebook co-founder <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Saverin" title="Eduardo Saverin">Eduardo Saverin</a> are two examples of wealthy individuals who have settled in Singapore (Blundy in 2013 and Saverin in 2012).<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup> Singapore ranked fifth on the <a href="/wiki/Tax_Justice_Network" title="Tax Justice Network">Tax Justice Network</a>'s 2013 <a href="/wiki/Financial_Secrecy_Index" title="Financial Secrecy Index">Financial Secrecy Index</a> of the world's top tax havens, scoring narrowly ahead of the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-FSI_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FSI-140">[139]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Singapore has the world's highest percentage of millionaires, with one out of every six households having at least one million US dollars in disposable wealth. This excludes property, businesses, and luxury goods, which if included would increase the number of millionaires, especially as property in Singapore is among the world's most expensive.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup> Singapore does not have a <a href="/wiki/Minimum_wage" title="Minimum wage">minimum wage</a>, believing that it would lower its competitiveness. It also has one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_income_equality" title="List of countries by income equality">highest income inequalities</a> among <a href="/wiki/Developed_countries" title="Developed countries" class="mw-redirect">developed countries</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[142]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry_sectors">Industry sectors</span></h3> 
     <p>Globally, Singapore is a leader in several economic sectors, including 3rd-largest <a href="/wiki/Foreign_exchange_market" title="Foreign exchange market">foreign exchange</a> centre, 4th-leading <a href="/wiki/Financial_centre" title="Financial centre">financial centre</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup> 2nd-largest casino gambling market,<sup id="cite_ref-edmontonjournal.com_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-edmontonjournal.com-145">[144]</a></sup> 3rd-largest oil-refining and trading centre, world's largest oil-rig producer and major hub for ship repair services,<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[146]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[147]</a></sup> world's top <a href="/wiki/Logistics" title="Logistics">logistics</a> hub.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:2012_Singapore_Products_Export_Treemap.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/2012_Singapore_Products_Export_Treemap.png/220px-2012_Singapore_Products_Export_Treemap.png" width="220" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/2012_Singapore_Products_Export_Treemap.png/330px-2012_Singapore_Products_Export_Treemap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/2012_Singapore_Products_Export_Treemap.png/440px-2012_Singapore_Products_Export_Treemap.png 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="582"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:2012_Singapore_Products_Export_Treemap.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Export treemap for 2012. Singapore is the world's 3rd largest 
        <a href="/wiki/Oil_refinery" title="Oil refinery">oil-refining</a> centre
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The economy is diversified, with its top contributors – financial services, manufacturing, oil-refining. Its main exports are refined petroleum, integrated circuits and computers <sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[149]</a></sup> which constituted 27% of the country's GDP in 2010, and includes significant electronics, petroleum refining, chemicals, <a href="/wiki/Mechanical_engineering" title="Mechanical engineering">mechanical engineering</a> and biomedical sciences sectors. In 2006, Singapore produced about 10% of the world's foundry <a href="/wiki/Wafer_(electronics)" title="Wafer (electronics)">wafer</a> output.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[150]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Singapore's largest companies are in the telecoms, banking, transportation and manufacturing sectors, many of which started as state-run enterprises, and has since been listed on the <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Exchange" title="Singapore Exchange">Singapore Exchange</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Telecommunications" title="Singapore Telecommunications" class="mw-redirect">Singapore Telecommunications</a> (Singtel), <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Technologies_Engineering" title="Singapore Technologies Engineering" class="mw-redirect">Singapore Technologies Engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Keppel_Corporation" title="Keppel Corporation">Keppel Corporation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oversea-Chinese_Banking_Corporation" title="Oversea-Chinese Banking Corporation">Oversea-Chinese Banking Corporation</a> (OCBC), <a href="/wiki/Development_Bank_of_Singapore" title="Development Bank of Singapore" class="mw-redirect">Development Bank of Singapore</a> (DBS), <a href="/wiki/United_Overseas_Bank" title="United Overseas Bank">United Overseas Bank</a> (UOB). In 2011, amidst the global financial crisis, OCBC, DBS and UOB were ranked as the world's 1st, 5th, 6th "strongest banks in the world" respectively by Bloomberg surveys.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[151]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The nation's best known global brands include <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Airlines" title="Singapore Airlines">Singapore Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Changi_Airport" title="Changi Airport" class="mw-redirect">Changi Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Singapore" title="Port of Singapore">Port of Singapore</a>, all three are amongst the most-awarded<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[note 1]</a></sup> in their respective industry sectors. Singapore Airlines is ranked as Asia's most-admired company, and world's 19th most-admired in 2015, by <a href="/wiki/Fortune_(magazine)" title="Fortune (magazine)">Fortune</a>'s annual "50 most admired companies in the world" industry surveys. It is also the world's most-awarded airline, including "Best international airline", by US-based <a href="/wiki/Travel_%2B_Leisure" title="Travel + Leisure">Travel + Leisure</a> reader surveys, for 20 consecutive years.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[152]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[153]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Changi_Airport" title="Changi Airport" class="mw-redirect">Changi Airport</a> connects over 100 airlines to more than 300 cities. The strategic international air hub has more than 480 "World's Best Airport" awards as of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, and is known as the most-awarded airport in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[154]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Universal_Singapore_Hollywood_Boulevard.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Universal_Singapore_Hollywood_Boulevard.jpg/220px-Universal_Singapore_Hollywood_Boulevard.jpg" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Universal_Singapore_Hollywood_Boulevard.jpg/330px-Universal_Singapore_Hollywood_Boulevard.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Universal_Singapore_Hollywood_Boulevard.jpg/440px-Universal_Singapore_Hollywood_Boulevard.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3983" data-file-height="2563"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Universal_Singapore_Hollywood_Boulevard.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Universal_Studios_Singapore" title="Universal Studios Singapore">Universal Studios</a>' Hollywood Boulevard, on 
        <a href="/wiki/Sentosa" title="Sentosa">Sentosa</a> island.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Singapore" title="Tourism in Singapore">Tourism</a> forms a large part of the economy, with over 15 million tourists visiting the city-state in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-singstat2014tourism_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singstat2014tourism-157">[155]</a></sup> To expand the sector, casinos were legalised in 2005, but only two licenses for "<a href="/wiki/Integrated_Resort" title="Integrated Resort" class="mw-redirect">Integrated Resorts</a>" were issued, to control money laundering and addiction.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[156]</a></sup> Singapore also promotes itself as a <a href="/wiki/Medical_tourism" title="Medical tourism">medical tourism</a> hub: about 200,000 foreigners seek medical care there each year. Singapore medical services aim to serve at least one million foreign patients annually and generate USD3&nbsp;billion in revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[157]</a></sup> In 2015, <a href="/wiki/Lonely_Planet" title="Lonely Planet">Lonely Planet</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a> listed Singapore as their top and 6th best world destination to visit respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[158]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Singapore is an education hub, with more than 80,000 international students in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[159]</a></sup> 5,000 Malaysian students cross the <a href="/wiki/Johor%E2%80%93Singapore_Causeway" title="Johor–Singapore Causeway">Johor–Singapore Causeway</a> daily to attend schools in Singapore.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[160]</a></sup> In 2009, 20% of all students in Singaporean universities were international students, a majority from ASEAN, China and India.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[161]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Singapore" title="Education in Singapore">Education in Singapore</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Singapore_Management_University_17,_Aug_06.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Singapore_Management_University_17%2C_Aug_06.JPG/220px-Singapore_Management_University_17%2C_Aug_06.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Singapore_Management_University_17%2C_Aug_06.JPG/330px-Singapore_Management_University_17%2C_Aug_06.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Singapore_Management_University_17%2C_Aug_06.JPG/440px-Singapore_Management_University_17%2C_Aug_06.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Singapore_Management_University_17,_Aug_06.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Management_University" title="Singapore Management University">Singapore Management University</a> is one of five 
        <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Singapore" title="List of universities in Singapore" class="mw-redirect">public universities in the city-state</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Education for primary, secondary, and tertiary levels is mostly supported by the state. All institutions, private and public, must be registered with the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Education_(Singapore)" title="Ministry of Education (Singapore)">Ministry of Education</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[162]</a></sup> English is the language of instruction in all public schools,<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[163]</a></sup> and all subjects are taught and examined in English except for the "<a href="/wiki/Mother_tongue" title="Mother tongue" class="mw-redirect">mother tongue</a>" language paper.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[164]</a></sup> While the term "mother tongue" in general refers to the first language internationally, in Singapore's education system, it is used to refer to the second language, as English is the first language.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[165]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[166]</a></sup> Students who have been abroad for a while, or who struggle with their "Mother Tongue" language, are allowed to take a simpler syllabus or drop the subject.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[167]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[168]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Education takes place in three stages: primary, secondary, and pre-university education. Only the primary level is compulsory. Students begin with six years of primary school, which is made up of a four-year foundation course and a two-year orientation stage. The curriculum is focused on the development of English, the mother tongue, <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">mathematics</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Natural_science" title="Natural science">science</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Primary_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Primary-171">[169]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[170]</a></sup> Secondary school lasts from four to five years, and is divided between Special, Express, Normal (Academic), and Normal (Technical) streams in each school, depending on a student's ability level.<sup id="cite_ref-Secondary_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Secondary-173">[171]</a></sup> The basic coursework breakdown is the same as in the primary level, although classes are much more specialised.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[172]</a></sup> Pre-university education takes place over two to three years at senior schools, mostly called <a href="/wiki/Junior_college_(Singapore)" title="Junior college (Singapore)">Junior Colleges</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Pre-university_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pre-university-175">[173]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Some schools have a degree of freedom in their curriculum and are known as autonomous schools. These exist from the <a href="/wiki/Secondary_education_in_Singapore" title="Secondary education in Singapore">secondary education</a> level and up.<sup id="cite_ref-Secondary_173-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Secondary-173">[171]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Hwa_Chong_Institution_Clock_Tower_Front_View.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Hwa_Chong_Institution_Clock_Tower_Front_View.JPG/220px-Hwa_Chong_Institution_Clock_Tower_Front_View.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Hwa_Chong_Institution_Clock_Tower_Front_View.JPG/330px-Hwa_Chong_Institution_Clock_Tower_Front_View.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Hwa_Chong_Institution_Clock_Tower_Front_View.JPG/440px-Hwa_Chong_Institution_Clock_Tower_Front_View.JPG 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Hwa_Chong_Institution_Clock_Tower_Front_View.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Hwa_Chong_Institution" title="Hwa Chong Institution">Hwa Chong Institution</a> was the first Chinese institution of higher learning in 
        <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> in 1919.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>National examinations are standardised across all schools, with a test taken after each stage. After the first six years of education, students take the <a href="/wiki/Primary_School_Leaving_Examination" title="Primary School Leaving Examination">Primary School Leaving Examination</a> (PSLE),<sup id="cite_ref-Primary_171-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Primary-171">[169]</a></sup> which determines their placement at secondary school. At the end of the secondary stage, <a href="/wiki/Singapore-Cambridge_GCE_Ordinary_Level" title="Singapore-Cambridge GCE Ordinary Level">GCE "O"-Level</a> exams are taken; at the end of the following pre-university stage, the <a href="/wiki/Singapore-Cambridge_GCE_Advanced_Level" title="Singapore-Cambridge GCE Advanced Level">GCE "A"-Level</a> exams are taken. Of all non-student Singaporeans aged 15 and above, 18% have no education qualifications at all while 45% have the PSLE as their highest qualification; 15% have the GCE 'O' Level as their highest qualification and 14% have a degree.<sup id="cite_ref-Chap2_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chap2-176">[174]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Singaporean students consistently rank at or near the top of international education assessments:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>In 2015, Singapore topped the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD's</a> global school performance rankings, based on 15-year-old students' average scores in mathematics and science across 76 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[175]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[176]</a></sup></li> 
      <li>Singaporean students were ranked first in the 2011 <a href="/wiki/Trends_in_International_Mathematics_and_Science_Study" title="Trends in International Mathematics and Science Study">Trends in International Mathematics and Science Study</a> conducted by the <a href="/wiki/International_Association_for_the_Evaluation_of_Educational_Achievement" title="International Association for the Evaluation of Educational Achievement">International Association for the Evaluation of Educational Achievement</a>, and have been ranked in the top three every year since 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[177]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[178]</a></sup></li> 
      <li>Singapore fared best in the 2015 <a href="/wiki/International_Baccalaureate" title="International Baccalaureate">International Baccalaureate</a> exams, taken in 107 countries, with more than half of the world's 81 perfect scorers and 98% passing rate.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[179]</a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>The country's two main public universities—the <a href="/wiki/National_University_of_Singapore" title="National University of Singapore">National University of Singapore</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nanyang_Technological_University" title="Nanyang Technological University">Nanyang Technological University</a>—are ranked among the top 13 in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[180]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Singapore" title="Healthcare in Singapore">Healthcare in Singapore</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Bowyer_Block,_SGH.JPG" class="image"><img alt="The Bowyer Block, Singapore General Hospital" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Bowyer_Block%2C_SGH.JPG/220px-Bowyer_Block%2C_SGH.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Bowyer_Block%2C_SGH.JPG/330px-Bowyer_Block%2C_SGH.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Bowyer_Block%2C_SGH.JPG/440px-Bowyer_Block%2C_SGH.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Bowyer_Block,_SGH.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Singapore_General_Hospital" title="Singapore General Hospital">Singapore General Hospital</a> Museum in housed in the "Bowyer Block"
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Singapore has a generally efficient healthcare system, even though their health expenditures are relatively low for developed countries.<sup id="cite_ref-Wyatt_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wyatt-183">[181]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organisation</a> ranks Singapore's healthcare system as 6th overall in the world in its <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Report" title="World Health Report">World Health Report</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WHO_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WHO-184">[182]</a></sup> In general, Singapore has had the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_infant_mortality_rate" title="List of countries by infant mortality rate">lowest infant mortality rate in the world</a> for the past two decades.<sup id="cite_ref-singstat2014births.26deaths_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singstat2014births.26deaths-185">[183]</a></sup> Life expectancy in Singapore is 80 for males and 85 for females, placing the country <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_life_expectancy#List_by_the_World_Health_Organization_.282011.29" title="List of countries by life expectancy">4th in the world for life expectancy</a>. Almost the whole population has access to improved water and <a href="/wiki/Sanitation" title="Sanitation">sanitation</a> facilities. There are fewer than 10 annual deaths from <a href="/wiki/HIV" title="HIV">HIV</a> per 100,000 people. There is a high level of <a href="/wiki/Immunisation" title="Immunisation" class="mw-redirect">immunisation</a>. Adult obesity is below 10%.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-186">[184]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The government's healthcare system is based upon the "3M" framework. This has three components: Medifund, which provides a safety net for those not able to otherwise afford healthcare, <a href="/wiki/Medisave" title="Medisave">Medisave</a>, a compulsory health savings scheme covering about 85% of the population, and Medishield, a government-funded health insurance program.<sup id="cite_ref-Wyatt_183-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wyatt-183">[181]</a></sup> Public hospitals in Singapore have autonomy in their management decisions, and compete for patients. A subsidy scheme exists for those on low income.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[185]</a></sup> In 2008, 32% of healthcare was funded by the government. It accounts for approximately 3.5% of Singapore's GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[186]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Information_and_communications">Information and communications</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:MICA_Building_13,_Feb_06.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/MICA_Building_13%2C_Feb_06.JPG/220px-MICA_Building_13%2C_Feb_06.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/MICA_Building_13%2C_Feb_06.JPG/330px-MICA_Building_13%2C_Feb_06.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/MICA_Building_13%2C_Feb_06.JPG/440px-MICA_Building_13%2C_Feb_06.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:MICA_Building_13,_Feb_06.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Communications_and_Information" title="Ministry of Communications and Information">Ministry of Communications and Information</a> oversees the development of Infocomms, Media and the Arts.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Information and communications technologies (ICT) is one of the pillars of Singapore's economic success. The <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">World Economic Forum</a>'s 2015 <a href="/wiki/Networked_Readiness_Index" title="Networked Readiness Index">Global Technology Report</a> placed Singapore as the most "Tech-Ready Nation". Its the most comprehensive survey of the pervasiveness and network-readiness of a country, in terms of market, political and regulatory infrastructure for connectivity. Singapore has also topped <a href="/wiki/Waseda_University" title="Waseda University">Waseda University</a>'s International e-Government rankings from 2009 to 2013, and 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-wef_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wef-189">[187]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Singapore has the world's highest <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">smartphone</a> penetration rates, in surveys by <a href="/wiki/Deloitte" title="Deloitte">Deloitte</a><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[188]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note--191">[189]</a></sup> and Google Consumer Barometer – at 89% and 85% of the population respectively in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[190]</a></sup> Overall <a href="/wiki/Mobile_phone" title="Mobile phone">mobile phone</a> penetration rate is at 148 mobile phone subscribers per 100 people.<sup id="cite_ref-singstat2014mobile_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singstat2014mobile-193">[191]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Internet_in_Singapore" title="Internet in Singapore">Internet in Singapore</a> is provided by state owned <a href="/wiki/Singtel" title="Singtel">Singtel</a> and partially state owned <a href="/wiki/Starhub" title="Starhub" class="mw-redirect">Starhub</a> and <a href="/wiki/M1_Limited" title="M1 Limited">M1 Limited</a> plus some other business <a href="/wiki/Internet_service_provider" title="Internet service provider">internet service providers</a> (ISPs) that offer residential service plans of speeds up to 2 <a href="/wiki/Gbit/s" title="Gbit/s" class="mw-redirect">Gbit/s</a> as of Spring 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[192]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Equinix" title="Equinix">Equinix</a> (332 participants) and also it's smaller brother <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Internet_Exchange" title="Singapore Internet Exchange">Singapore Internet Exchange</a> (70 participants) are <a href="/wiki/Internet_exchange_point" title="Internet exchange point">Internet exchange points</a> where <a href="/wiki/Internet_service_provider" title="Internet service provider">Internet service providers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Content_delivery_network" title="Content delivery network">Content delivery networks</a> exchange Internet traffic between their networks (<a href="/wiki/Autonomous_system_(Internet)" title="Autonomous system (Internet)">autonomous systems</a>) in various locations in Singapore.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Singapore" title="Transport in Singapore">Transport in Singapore</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:027_ERP_gantry.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/027_ERP_gantry.jpg/220px-027_ERP_gantry.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/027_ERP_gantry.jpg/330px-027_ERP_gantry.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/027_ERP_gantry.jpg/440px-027_ERP_gantry.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:027_ERP_gantry.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Electronic Road Pricing 
        <a href="/wiki/Gantry_(road_sign)" title="Gantry (road sign)">gantry (road sign)</a> at 
        <a href="/wiki/Beach_Road,_Singapore" title="Beach Road, Singapore">Beach Road</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>As Singapore is a small island with a high population density, the number of private cars on the road is restricted so as to curb pollution and congestion. Car buyers must pay for duties one-and-a-half times the vehicle's market value, and bid for a Singaporean <a href="/wiki/Certificate_of_Entitlement" title="Certificate of Entitlement">Certificate of Entitlement</a> (COE), which allows the car to run on the road for a decade. The cost of the Singaporean certificate of entitlement alone would buy a <a href="/wiki/Porsche_Boxster" title="Porsche Boxster" class="mw-redirect">Porsche Boxster</a> in the United States. Car prices are generally significantly higher in Singapore than in other English-speaking countries.<sup id="cite_ref-BloombergBMW_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BloombergBMW-195">[193]</a></sup> As with most Commonwealth countries, vehicles on the road and people walking on the streets keep to the left.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[194]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Singaporean residents also travel by foot, bicycles, <a href="/wiki/Bus_transport_in_Singapore" title="Bus transport in Singapore">bus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taxis" title="Taxis">taxis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Train" title="Train">train</a> (<a href="/wiki/Mass_Rapid_Transit_(Singapore)" title="Mass Rapid Transit (Singapore)">MRT</a> or <a href="/wiki/Light_Rail_Transit_(Singapore)" title="Light Rail Transit (Singapore)">LRT</a>). Two companies run the public bus and train transport system—<a href="/wiki/SBS_Transit" title="SBS Transit">SBS Transit</a> and <a href="/wiki/SMRT_Corporation" title="SMRT Corporation">SMRT Corporation</a>. There are six <a href="/wiki/Taxicabs_of_Singapore" title="Taxicabs of Singapore">taxi companies</a>, who together put out over 28,000 taxis on the road.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[195]</a></sup> Taxis are a popular form of public transport as the fares are relatively cheap compared to many other developed countries.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[196]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Singapore has a <a href="/wiki/Road_transport_in_Singapore" title="Road transport in Singapore" class="mw-redirect">road system</a> covering 3,356 kilometres (2,085&nbsp;mi), which includes 161 kilometres (100&nbsp;mi) <a href="/wiki/Expressways_of_Singapore" title="Expressways of Singapore">of expressways</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[197]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[198]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Area_Licensing_Scheme" title="Singapore Area Licensing Scheme">Singapore Area Licensing Scheme</a>, implemented in 1975, became the world's first <a href="/wiki/Congestion_pricing" title="Congestion pricing">congestion pricing</a> scheme, and included other complementary measures such as stringent car ownership quotas and improvements in mass transit.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[199]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[200]</a></sup> Upgraded in 1998 and renamed <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Road_Pricing" title="Electronic Road Pricing">Electronic Road Pricing</a>, the system introduced <a href="/wiki/Electronic_toll_collection" title="Electronic toll collection">electronic toll collection</a>, electronic detection, and video surveillance technology.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[201]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Singapore_Changi_Airport,_Control_Tower_2,_Dec_05.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Singapore_Changi_Airport%2C_Control_Tower_2%2C_Dec_05.JPG/220px-Singapore_Changi_Airport%2C_Control_Tower_2%2C_Dec_05.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Singapore_Changi_Airport%2C_Control_Tower_2%2C_Dec_05.JPG/330px-Singapore_Changi_Airport%2C_Control_Tower_2%2C_Dec_05.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Singapore_Changi_Airport%2C_Control_Tower_2%2C_Dec_05.JPG/440px-Singapore_Changi_Airport%2C_Control_Tower_2%2C_Dec_05.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Singapore_Changi_Airport,_Control_Tower_2,_Dec_05.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Changi_Airport" title="Changi Airport" class="mw-redirect">Changi Airport</a> continues to expand with a 4th Terminal and mixed-use complex Jewel by 2018
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Singapore is a major international <a href="/wiki/Transport_hub" title="Transport hub">transport hub</a> in Asia, serving some of the busiest sea and air trade routes. <a href="/wiki/Changi_Airport" title="Changi Airport" class="mw-redirect">Changi Airport</a> is an aviation centre for Southeast Asia and a stopover on the <a href="/wiki/Kangaroo_Route" title="Kangaroo Route">Kangaroo Route</a> between <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a> and London.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[202]</a></sup> There are eight airports in the country, and <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Changi_Airport" title="Singapore Changi Airport">Singapore Changi Airport</a> hosts a network of over 100 airlines connecting Singapore to some 300 cities in about 70 countries and territories worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[203]</a></sup> It has been rated one of the best international airports by international travel magazines, including being rated as the world's best airport for the first time in 2006 by <a href="/wiki/Skytrax" title="Skytrax">Skytrax</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[204]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Flag_carrier" title="Flag carrier">national airline</a> is <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Airlines" title="Singapore Airlines">Singapore Airlines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[205]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Singapore" title="Port of Singapore">Port of Singapore</a>, managed by port operators <a href="/wiki/PSA_International" title="PSA International">PSA International</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jurong_Port" title="Jurong Port">Jurong Port</a>, was the world's second-busiest port in 2005 in terms of <a href="/wiki/Shipping" title="Shipping" class="mw-redirect">shipping</a> tonnage handled, at 1.15&nbsp;billion <a href="/wiki/Gross_ton" title="Gross ton" class="mw-redirect">gross tons</a>, and in terms of <a href="/wiki/Container_(cargo)" title="Container (cargo)" class="mw-redirect">containerised</a> traffic, at 23.2&nbsp;million <a href="/wiki/Twenty-foot_equivalent_unit" title="Twenty-foot equivalent unit">twenty-foot equivalent units</a> (TEUs). It is also the world's second-busiest, behind Shanghai, in terms of cargo tonnage with 423&nbsp;million tons handled. In addition, the port is the world's busiest for <a href="/wiki/Transshipment" title="Transshipment">transshipment</a> traffic and the world's biggest ship refuelling centre.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[206]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="center"> 
      <div class="thumb tnone"> 
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:802px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Singapore_port_panorama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="The Port with a large number of shipping containers and the ocean visible in the background" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Singapore_port_panorama.jpg/800px-Singapore_port_panorama.jpg" width="800" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Singapore_port_panorama.jpg/1200px-Singapore_port_panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Singapore_port_panorama.jpg/1600px-Singapore_port_panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="10000" data-file-height="1842"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption"> 
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Singapore_port_panorama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div> The 
         <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Singapore" title="Port of Singapore">Port of Singapore</a>, one of the top two 
         <a href="/wiki/List_of_world%27s_busiest_container_ports" title="List of world's busiest container ports">busiest container ports in the world</a> since the 1990s. Sentosa island in the background
        </div> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_supply_and_sanitation">Water supply and sanitation</span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Singapore" title="Water supply and sanitation in Singapore">Water supply and sanitation in Singapore</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Access to water is universal, affordable, efficient and of high quality. Innovative integrated water management approaches such as the reuse of <a href="/wiki/Reclaimed_water" title="Reclaimed water">reclaimed water</a>, the establishment of protected areas in urban rainwater catchments and the use of estuaries as freshwater reservoirs have been introduced along with seawater <a href="/wiki/Desalination" title="Desalination">desalination</a> to reduce the country's dependence on water imported from neighbouring Malaysia.</p> 
     <p>Singapore's approach does not rely only on physical infrastructure, but it also emphasises proper legislation and enforcement, water pricing, public education as well as research and development.<sup id="cite_ref-Luan_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Luan-209">[207]</a></sup> In 2007 Singapore's water and sanitation utility, the <a href="/wiki/Public_Utilities_Board" title="Public Utilities Board">Public Utilities Board</a>, received the <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Industry_Water_Award" title="Stockholm Industry Water Award">Stockholm Industry Water Award</a> for its holistic approach to water resources management.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[208]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Singapore" title="Demographics of Singapore">Demographics of Singapore</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Singaporeans" title="Singaporeans">Singaporeans</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:1_bishan_park_panorama_2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/1_bishan_park_panorama_2012.jpg/290px-1_bishan_park_panorama_2012.jpg" width="290" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/1_bishan_park_panorama_2012.jpg/435px-1_bishan_park_panorama_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/1_bishan_park_panorama_2012.jpg/580px-1_bishan_park_panorama_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="10192" data-file-height="4352"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:1_bishan_park_panorama_2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> High-rise HDB flats and 
        <a href="/wiki/Condominium" title="Condominium">condominiums</a> overlooking 
        <a href="/wiki/Bishan-Ang_Mo_Kio_Park" title="Bishan-Ang Mo Kio Park">Bishan-Ang Mo Kio Park</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>As of mid-2015, the estimated population of Singapore was 5,535,000 people, 3,375,000 (60.98%) of whom were <a href="/wiki/Singaporean_nationality_law" title="Singaporean nationality law">citizens</a>, while the remaining 2,160,000 (39.02%) were <a href="/wiki/Permanent_residents" title="Permanent residents" class="mw-redirect">permanent residents</a> (527,700) or <a href="/wiki/Foreign_student" title="Foreign student" class="mw-redirect">foreign students</a>/<a href="/wiki/Foreign_worker" title="Foreign worker">foreign workers</a>/<a href="/wiki/Dependant" title="Dependant">dependants</a> (1,632,300).<sup id="cite_ref-singstat2015pop.26land_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singstat2015pop.26land-10">[9]</a></sup> According to the country's most recent census in 2010, nearly 23% of Singaporean residents (i.e. citizens and permanent residents) were <a href="/wiki/Foreign_born" title="Foreign born">foreign born</a> (which means about 10% of Singapore citizens were foreign-born <a href="/wiki/Naturalised" title="Naturalised" class="mw-redirect">naturalised</a> citizens); if non-residents were counted, nearly 43% of the total population were foreign born.<sup id="cite_ref-2010census_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010census-211">[209]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-un.org_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-un.org-212">[210]</a></sup> The same census also reports that about 74.1% of residents were of Chinese descent, 13.4% of Malay descent, 9.2% of Indian descent, and 3.3% of other (including <a href="/wiki/Eurasians_in_Singapore" title="Eurasians in Singapore">Eurasian</a>) descent.<sup id="cite_ref-2010census_211-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010census-211">[209]</a></sup> Prior to 2010, each person could register as a member of only one race, by default that of his or her father, therefore mixed-race persons were solely grouped under their father's race in government censuses. From 2010 onward, people may register using a multi-racial classification, in which they may choose one primary race and one secondary race, but no more than two.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[211]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>90.3% of resident households (i.e. households headed by a Singapore citizen or permanent resident) own the homes they live in, and the average household size is 3.43 persons (which include dependants who are neither citizens nor permanent residents).<sup id="cite_ref-singstat2014h.26h_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singstat2014h.26h-214">[212]</a></sup> However, due to scarcity of land, 80.4% of resident households live in <a href="/wiki/Public_housing_in_Singapore" title="Public housing in Singapore">subsidised, high-rise, public housing apartments</a> known as "HDB flats" because of the government board (<a href="/wiki/Housing_and_Development_Board" title="Housing and Development Board">Housing and Development Board</a>) responsible for public housing in the country. Also, 75.9% of resident households live in properties that are equal to, or larger than, a four-room (i.e. three bedrooms plus one living room) HDB flat or in private housing.<sup id="cite_ref-singstat2014h.26h_214-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singstat2014h.26h-214">[212]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hdb_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdb-215">[213]</a></sup> Live-in foreign <a href="/wiki/Domestic_worker" title="Domestic worker">domestic workers</a> are quite common in Singapore, with about 224,500 foreign domestic workers there, as of December 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[214]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The median age of Singaporean residents is 39.3,<sup id="cite_ref-singstat2014respoppro_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singstat2014respoppro-217">[215]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> is estimated to be 0.80 children per woman in 2014, the lowest in the world and well below the 2.1 needed to replace the population.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[216]</a></sup> To overcome this problem, the Singapore government has been encouraging foreigners to immigrate to Singapore for the past few decades. The large number of immigrants has kept Singapore's population from declining.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[217]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Singapore" title="Religion in Singapore">Religion in Singapore</a>
     </div>

          </div> </td>

      </table> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_Singapore" title="Buddhism in Singapore">Buddhism</a> is the most widely practised religion in Singapore, with 33% of the resident population declaring themselves adherents at the most recent census. The next-most practised religion is <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Singapore" title="Christianity in Singapore">Christianity</a>, followed by <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Singapore" title="Islam in Singapore">Islam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taoism_in_Singapore" title="Taoism in Singapore">Taoism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_Singapore" title="Hinduism in Singapore">Hinduism</a>. 17% of the population did not have a religious affiliation. The proportion of Christians, Taoists, and non-religious people increased between 2000 and 2010 by about 3% each, whilst the proportion of Buddhists decreased. Other faiths remained largely stable in their share of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-2010censuspercentage_220-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010censuspercentage-220">[218]</a></sup> An analysis by the <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a> found Singapore to be the world's most religiously diverse nation.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[219]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pew_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pew-222">[220]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>There are monasteries and <a href="/wiki/Dharma" title="Dharma">Dharma</a> centres from all three major traditions of Buddhism in Singapore: <a href="/wiki/Theravada" title="Theravada">Theravada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mahayana" title="Mahayana">Mahayana</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vajrayana" title="Vajrayana">Vajrayana</a>. Most Buddhists in Singapore are Chinese and are of the Mahayana tradition,<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[221]</a></sup> with missionaries having come into the country from Taiwan and China for several decades. However, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_Thailand" title="Buddhism in Thailand">Thailand's Theravada Buddhism</a> has seen growing popularity among the populace (not only the Chinese) during the past decade. <a href="/wiki/Soka_Gakkai_International" title="Soka Gakkai International">Soka Gakkai International</a>, a Japanese Buddhist organisation, is practised by many people in Singapore, but mostly by those of Chinese descent. <a href="/wiki/Tibetan_Buddhism" title="Tibetan Buddhism">Tibetan Buddhism</a> has also made slow inroads into the country in recent years.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[222]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Singapore" title="Languages of Singapore">Languages of Singapore</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:A_warning_sign_in_Singapore%27s_construction_site.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/A_warning_sign_in_Singapore%27s_construction_site.jpg/170px-A_warning_sign_in_Singapore%27s_construction_site.jpg" width="170" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/A_warning_sign_in_Singapore%27s_construction_site.jpg/255px-A_warning_sign_in_Singapore%27s_construction_site.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/A_warning_sign_in_Singapore%27s_construction_site.jpg/340px-A_warning_sign_in_Singapore%27s_construction_site.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:A_warning_sign_in_Singapore%27s_construction_site.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> A warning sign in 4 official languages ( including 
        <a href="/wiki/Traditional_Chinese" title="Traditional Chinese" class="mw-redirect">traditional Chinese</a>) at a construction site.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Singapore has four official languages: English, Malay, Mandarin Chinese, and <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-statutes.agc.gov.sg_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statutes.agc.gov.sg-225">[223]</a></sup> English is the common language, and is the language of business, government, and the medium of instruction in schools.<sup id="cite_ref-Britishcouncil_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britishcouncil-226">[224]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[225]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Public_bodies" title="Public bodies" class="mw-redirect">Public bodies</a> in Singapore, such as the Singapore Public Service, (which includes the <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Civil_Service" title="Singapore Civil Service">Singapore Civil Service</a> and other agencies),<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[226]</a></sup> conduct their business in English, and official documents written in a non-English official language such as Malay, Chinese or Tamil typically have to be <a href="/wiki/Translation" title="Translation">translated</a> into English to be accepted for submission. The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Singapore" title="Constitution of Singapore">Constitution of Singapore</a> and all laws are written in English,<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[227]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Language_interpretation" title="Language interpretation">interpreters</a> are required if one wishes to address the <a href="/wiki/Judicial_system_of_Singapore" title="Judicial system of Singapore">Singaporean Courts</a> in a language other than English.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[228]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[229]</a></sup> English is the native tongue for only one-third of all Singaporeans, with roughly a quarter of all Singaporean Malays, a third of all Singaporean Chinese, and half of all Singaporean Indians speaking it as their native tongue. Twenty percent of Singaporeans cannot read or write in English.<sup id="cite_ref-2010censuspercentage_220-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010censuspercentage-220">[218]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-232">[230]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="barbox tright" style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;"> 
      <table style="border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr style="background:#ddd"> 
         <th colspan="5">Native languages of Singaporeans<sup id="cite_ref-singstat1_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singstat1-233">[231]</a></sup></th> 
        </tr> 
        <tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;"> 
         <td style="padding:0 4px;">Language</td> 
         <td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:right;"></td> 
         <td style="width:100px;"></td>

        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Mandarin Chinese</td>

          <div style="background:yellow; width:50%; overflow: hidden;">
           &nbsp; 
          </div> </td> 
         <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">50%</td> 
        </tr>
