          </div> </td> 
         <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">32%</td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Malay</td> 
         <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"> 
          <div style="background:grey; width:12%; overflow: hidden;">
           &nbsp; 
          </div> </td> 
         <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">12%</td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Tamil</td> 
         <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"> 
          <div style="background:green; width:3%; overflow: hidden;">
           &nbsp; 
          </div> </td> 
         <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">3%</td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div> 
     <p>Singaporeans are mostly <a href="/wiki/Bilingual" title="Bilingual" class="mw-redirect">bilingual</a>, with <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> as their common language and usually the <a href="/wiki/Mother-tongue" title="Mother-tongue" class="mw-redirect">mother-tongue</a> as a second language taught in schools, in order to preserve each individual's ethnic identity and values. The official languages amongst Singaporeans are English (80% literacy), Mandarin (65% literacy), Malay (17% literacy), and Tamil (4% literacy).<sup id="cite_ref-2010censuspercentage_220-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010censuspercentage-220">[218]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[232]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Singapore_English" title="Singapore English">Singapore English</a> is based on <a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">British English</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[233]</a></sup> and forms of English spoken in Singapore range from <a href="/wiki/Singapore_English#Standard_Singapore_English" title="Singapore English">Standard Singapore English</a> to a <a href="/wiki/Pidgin" title="Pidgin">pidgin</a> known as "<a href="/wiki/Singlish" title="Singlish">Singlish</a>". Singlish is discouraged by the government.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[234]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Teochew_Building,_Mar_06.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Teochew_Building%2C_Mar_06.JPG/150px-Teochew_Building%2C_Mar_06.JPG" width="150" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Teochew_Building%2C_Mar_06.JPG/225px-Teochew_Building%2C_Mar_06.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Teochew_Building%2C_Mar_06.JPG/300px-Teochew_Building%2C_Mar_06.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1600"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Teochew_Building,_Mar_06.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Clan associations played an important role in preserving ethnic dialects and cultural practices in the early years.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Mandarin_Chinese" title="Mandarin Chinese">Mandarin</a> is the language that is spoken as the native tongue by the greatest number of Singaporeans, half of them.<sup id="cite_ref-singstat1_233-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singstat1-233">[231]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Singaporean_Mandarin" title="Singaporean Mandarin">Singaporean Mandarin</a> is the most common version of Chinese in the country,<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-237">[235]</a></sup> with 1.2&nbsp;million using it as their home language. Nearly half a million speak other <a href="/wiki/Varieties_of_Chinese" title="Varieties of Chinese">varieties of Chinese</a>, mainly <a href="/wiki/Hokkien" title="Hokkien">Hokkien</a>, <a href="/wiki/Teochew_dialect" title="Teochew dialect">Teochew</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cantonese" title="Cantonese">Cantonese</a>, as their home language, although the use of these is declining in favour of Mandarin and English.<sup id="cite_ref-singstat.gov.sg_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singstat.gov.sg-238">[236]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">Malay</a> was chosen as a national language by the Singaporean government after independence from Britain in the 1960s to avoid friction with Singapore's Malay-speaking neighbours—Malaysia and Indonesia.<sup id="cite_ref-fromthirdworldtofirst_239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fromthirdworldtofirst-239">[237]</a></sup> It has a symbolic, rather than functional purpose.<sup id="cite_ref-statutes.agc.gov.sg_225-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statutes.agc.gov.sg-225">[223]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">[238]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">[239]</a></sup> It is used in the national anthem "Majulah Singapura",<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">[240]</a></sup> in citations of <a href="/wiki/Singaporean_orders_and_decorations" title="Singaporean orders and decorations">Singaporean orders and decorations</a>, and in military commands. In general, Malay is spoken mainly within the Singaporean Malay community, with only 17% of all Singaporeans literate in Malay<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">[241]</a></sup> and only 12% using it as their native language.<sup id="cite_ref-singstat1_233-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singstat1-233">[231]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Around 100,000, or 3%, of Singaporeans speak Tamil as their native language.<sup id="cite_ref-singstat1_233-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singstat1-233">[231]</a></sup> Tamil has official status in Singapore and there have been no attempts to discourage the use of other Indian languages.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">[242]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Employment">Employment</span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Employment_in_Singapore" title="Employment in Singapore">Employment in Singapore</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Singapore traditionally has one of the lowest <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_unemployment_rate" title="List of countries by unemployment rate">unemployment rates</a> among developed countries. The unemployment rate did not exceed 4% from 2005 to 2014, hitting highs of 3.1% in 2005 and 3% during the <a href="/wiki/Late-2000s_financial_crisis" title="Late-2000s financial crisis" class="mw-redirect">2009 global financial crisis</a>; it fell to 1.8% in the first quarter of 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">[243]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The government provides numerous assistance programmes to the homeless and needy through the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Social_and_Family_Development" title="Ministry of Social and Family Development">Ministry of Social and Family Development</a>, so acute poverty is rare. Some of the programmes include providing between SGD400 and SGD1000 per month to needy households, providing free medical care at government hospitals, and paying for children's school fees.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">[244]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">[245]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">[246]</a></sup> The Singapore government also provides numerous benefits to its citizenry, including: free money to encourage residents to exercise in public gyms,<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">[247]</a></sup> up to $166,000 worth of <a href="/wiki/Baby_bonus" title="Baby bonus">baby bonus</a> benefits for each baby born to a citizen,<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">[248]</a></sup> heavily subsidised healthcare, money to help the disabled, cheap laptops for poor students,<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">[249]</a></sup> rebates for numerous areas such as public transport,<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">[250]</a></sup> utility bills and more.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">[251]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">[252]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Although it has been recognised that foreign workers are crucial to the country's economy, the government is considering capping these workers,<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">[253]</a></sup> as foreign workers make up 80% of the construction industry and up to 50% of the service industry.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">[254]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">[255]</a></sup> To keep an effective tap on the issue of immigration and to also attract foreign talents at the same time, the Ministry of Manpower (MoM) issues employment pass under three categories viz: P1 Employment Pass for those individuals with monthly earning of $8,000 and up, P2 Employment Pass for individuals with monthly earning of $4,500–7,999 and Q1 Employment Pass individuals with at least a monthly earning of $3,000.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">[256]</a></sup></p> 
     <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
     <div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:100%; max-width:1708px;"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style=""> 
       <div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Panoramic_view_of_the_Central_Business_District,_Singapore,_and_ships_-_20100712.jpg" class="image" title="Cityscape from Singapore's Eastern Anchorage off the East Coast Park"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Panoramic_view_of_the_Central_Business_District%2C_Singapore%2C_and_ships_-_20100712.jpg/1700px-Panoramic_view_of_the_Central_Business_District%2C_Singapore%2C_and_ships_-_20100712.jpg" width="1700" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Panoramic_view_of_the_Central_Business_District%2C_Singapore%2C_and_ships_-_20100712.jpg/2550px-Panoramic_view_of_the_Central_Business_District%2C_Singapore%2C_and_ships_-_20100712.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Panoramic_view_of_the_Central_Business_District%2C_Singapore%2C_and_ships_-_20100712.jpg/3400px-Panoramic_view_of_the_Central_Business_District%2C_Singapore%2C_and_ships_-_20100712.jpg 2x" data-file-width="20414" data-file-height="1806"></a>
       </div> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Panoramic_view_of_the_Central_Business_District,_Singapore,_and_ships_-_20100712.jpg" title="File:Panoramic view of the Central Business District, Singapore, and ships - 20100712.jpg"></a>
        </div> Cityscape from Singapore's Eastern Anchorage off the 
        <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_Park" title="East Coast Park">East Coast Park</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Singapore" title="Culture of Singapore">Culture of Singapore</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Singapore has one of the lowest rates of drug use in the world. Culturally, the use of illicit drugs is viewed as highly undesirable by Singaporeans, unlike many European societies. Singaporeans' disapproval towards drug use has resulted in laws that impose the <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_death_sentence" title="Mandatory death sentence" class="mw-redirect">mandatory death sentence</a> for certain serious <a href="/wiki/Drug_trafficking" title="Drug trafficking" class="mw-redirect">drug trafficking</a> offences. Singapore also has a low rate of alcohol consumption per capita and low levels of violent crime, and one of the lowest <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_intentional_homicide_rate" title="List of countries by intentional homicide rate">intentional homicide rate</a> globally. The average alcohol consumption rate is only 2 litres annually per adult, one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_alcohol_consumption_per_capita" title="List of countries by alcohol consumption per capita">lowest in the world</a>.</p> 
     <p>Foreigners make up 42% of the population,<sup id="cite_ref-un.org_212-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-un.org-212">[210]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-singstat.gov.sg_238-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singstat.gov.sg-238">[236]</a></sup> and have a strong influence on Singaporean culture. The <a href="/wiki/Economist_Intelligence_Unit" title="Economist Intelligence Unit">Economist Intelligence Unit</a>, in its 2013 "<a href="/wiki/Where-to-be-born_Index#2013_rankings" title="Where-to-be-born Index">Where-to-be-born Index</a>", ranks Singapore as having the best quality of life in Asia and sixth overall in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">[257]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages.2C_religions.2C_and_cultures">Languages, religions, and cultures</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Chinese_New_Year_market.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Chinese_New_Year_market.jpg/220px-Chinese_New_Year_market.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Chinese_New_Year_market.jpg/330px-Chinese_New_Year_market.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Chinese_New_Year_market.jpg/440px-Chinese_New_Year_market.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Chinese_New_Year_market.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> A scene in a street market in 
        <a href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Singapore" title="Chinatown, Singapore">Chinatown, Singapore</a>, during the 
        <a href="/wiki/Chinese_New_Year" title="Chinese New Year">Chinese New Year</a> holidays.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:A_day_of_devotion_%E2%80%93_Thaipusam_in_Singapore_(4316108409).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/A_day_of_devotion_%E2%80%93_Thaipusam_in_Singapore_%284316108409%29.jpg/220px-A_day_of_devotion_%E2%80%93_Thaipusam_in_Singapore_%284316108409%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/A_day_of_devotion_%E2%80%93_Thaipusam_in_Singapore_%284316108409%29.jpg/330px-A_day_of_devotion_%E2%80%93_Thaipusam_in_Singapore_%284316108409%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/A_day_of_devotion_%E2%80%93_Thaipusam_in_Singapore_%284316108409%29.jpg/440px-A_day_of_devotion_%E2%80%93_Thaipusam_in_Singapore_%284316108409%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1417" data-file-height="948"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:A_day_of_devotion_%E2%80%93_Thaipusam_in_Singapore_(4316108409).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Thaipusam" title="Thaipusam">Thaipusam</a> procession in Singapore
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Armenian_Church,_Singapore,_Jan_06.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Armenian_Church%2C_Singapore%2C_Jan_06.JPG/220px-Armenian_Church%2C_Singapore%2C_Jan_06.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Armenian_Church%2C_Singapore%2C_Jan_06.JPG/330px-Armenian_Church%2C_Singapore%2C_Jan_06.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Armenian_Church%2C_Singapore%2C_Jan_06.JPG/440px-Armenian_Church%2C_Singapore%2C_Jan_06.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Armenian_Church,_Singapore,_Jan_06.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Church,_Singapore" title="Armenian Church, Singapore">Armenian Church of Saint Gregory the Illuminator</a>—the oldest Christian church in Singapore
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:The_Sultan_Mosque_at_Kampong_Glam,_Singapore_(8125148933).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/The_Sultan_Mosque_at_Kampong_Glam%2C_Singapore_%288125148933%29.jpg/220px-The_Sultan_Mosque_at_Kampong_Glam%2C_Singapore_%288125148933%29.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/The_Sultan_Mosque_at_Kampong_Glam%2C_Singapore_%288125148933%29.jpg/330px-The_Sultan_Mosque_at_Kampong_Glam%2C_Singapore_%288125148933%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/The_Sultan_Mosque_at_Kampong_Glam%2C_Singapore_%288125148933%29.jpg/440px-The_Sultan_Mosque_at_Kampong_Glam%2C_Singapore_%288125148933%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2464" data-file-height="1656"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:The_Sultan_Mosque_at_Kampong_Glam,_Singapore_(8125148933).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Masjid_Sultan" title="Masjid Sultan">Sultan Mosque</a> in Singapore
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Singapore is a very diverse and young country. It has many languages, religions, and cultures for a country its size.<sup id="cite_ref-singapore21_260-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singapore21-260">[258]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>When Singapore became independent from the United Kingdom in 1963, most of the newly minted Singaporean citizens were uneducated labourers from Malaysia, China and <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>. Many of them were transient labourers who were seeking to make some money in Singapore and they had no intention of staying permanently. A sizeable minority of middle-class, local-born people, known as the <a href="/wiki/Peranakan" title="Peranakan">Peranakans</a>, also existed. With the exception of the Peranakans (descendants of late 15th and 16th-century Chinese immigrants) who pledged their loyalties to Singapore, most of the labourers' loyalties lay with their respective homelands of Malaysia, China and India.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">[259]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">[260]</a></sup> After independence, the process of crafting a Singaporean identity and culture began.</p> 
     <p>Former Prime Ministers of Singapore, Lee Kuan Yew and Goh Chok Tong, have stated that Singapore does not fit the traditional description of a <a href="/wiki/Nation" title="Nation">nation</a>, calling it a society-in-transition, pointing out the fact that Singaporeans do not all speak the same language, share the same religion, or have the same customs.<sup id="cite_ref-singapore21_260-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singapore21-260">[258]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">[261]</a></sup> Even though English is the first language of the nation, according to the government's 2010 census 20% of Singaporeans, or one in five, are <a href="/wiki/Illiterate" title="Illiterate" class="mw-redirect">illiterate</a> in English. This is a marked improvement from 1990 where 40% of Singaporeans were illiterate in English.<sup id="cite_ref-singstat_a_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singstat_a-264">[262]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">[263]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Languages, religions and cultures among Singaporeans are not delineated according to <a href="/wiki/Skin_colour" title="Skin colour" class="mw-redirect">skin colour</a> or <a href="/wiki/Ancestry" title="Ancestry" class="mw-redirect">ancestry</a>, unlike many other countries. Among Chinese Singaporeans, one in five is <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">Christian</a>, another one in five is <a href="/wiki/Atheist" title="Atheist" class="mw-redirect">atheist</a>, and the rest are mostly <a href="/wiki/Buddhists" title="Buddhists" class="mw-redirect">Buddhists</a> or <a href="/wiki/Taoists" title="Taoists" class="mw-redirect">Taoists</a>. One-third speak English as their home language, while half speak Mandarin Chinese. The rest speak other Chinese varieties at home. Most Malays in Singapore speak Malay as their home language with some speaking English.<sup id="cite_ref-singstat_a_264-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singstat_a-264">[262]</a></sup> Singaporean Indians are much more religious. Only 1% of them are atheists. Six in ten are Hindu, two in ten Muslim, and the rest mostly Christian. Four in ten speak English as their home language, three in ten <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a>, one in ten Malay, and the rest other <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_India" title="Languages of India">Indian languages</a> as their home language.<sup id="cite_ref-singstat_a_264-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singstat_a-264">[262]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Each Singaporean's behaviours and attitudes would therefore be influenced by, among many other things, his or her home <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">language</a> and his <a href="/wiki/Religion" title="Religion">religion</a>. Singaporeans who speak English as their native language tend to lean toward <a href="/wiki/Western_culture" title="Western culture">Western culture</a>, while those who speak Chinese as their native language tend to lean toward <a href="/wiki/Chinese_culture" title="Chinese culture">Chinese culture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">Confucianism</a>. Malay speaking Singaporeans tend to lean toward the <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_Malays" title="Ethnic Malays" class="mw-redirect">Malay culture</a>, which itself is closely linked to the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_culture" title="Islamic culture">Islamic culture</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Attitudes_and_beliefs">Attitudes and beliefs</span></h3> 
     <p>At the national level in Singapore, <a href="/wiki/Meritocracy" title="Meritocracy">meritocracy</a>, where one is judged based on one's ability, is heavily emphasised.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">[264]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Racial and religious harmony is regarded by Singaporeans as a crucial part of Singapore's success, and played a part in building a Singaporean identity.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">[265]</a></sup> Singapore has a reputation as a <a href="/wiki/Nanny_state" title="Nanny state">nanny state</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">[266]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">[267]</a></sup> The national flower of Singapore is the <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_(biology)#Hybrid_plants" title="Hybrid (biology)">hybrid</a> <a href="/wiki/Orchid" title="Orchid" class="mw-redirect">orchid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vanda_%27Miss_Joaquim%27" title="Vanda 'Miss Joaquim'">Vanda 'Miss Joaquim'</a>, named in memory of a Singapore-born <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">Armenian</a> woman, who crossbred the flower in her garden at <a href="/wiki/Tanjong_Pagar" title="Tanjong Pagar">Tanjong Pagar</a> in 1893.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">[268]</a></sup> Many national symbols such as the <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Singapore" title="Coat of arms of Singapore">Coat of arms of Singapore</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Lion_head_symbol_of_Singapore" title="Lion head symbol of Singapore">Lion head symbol of Singapore</a> make use of the <a href="/wiki/Lion" title="Lion">lion</a>, as Singapore is known as the <i>Lion City</i>. Other monikers by which Singapore is widely known is the <i>Garden City</i> and the <i>Red Dot</i>. <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Singapore" title="Public holidays in Singapore">Public holidays in Singapore</a> cover major Chinese, Western, Malay and Indian festivals.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">[269]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Singaporean employees work an average of around 45 hours weekly, relatively long compared to many other nations. Three in four Singaporean employees surveyed stated that they take pride in doing their work well, and that doing so helps their self-confidence.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">[270]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Singaporean_cuisine" title="Singaporean cuisine">Singaporean cuisine</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Satay_stalls_along_Boon_Tat_Street_next_to_Telok_Ayer_Market,_Singapore_-_20120629-02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Satay stalls along Boon Tat Street next to Telok Ayer Market, better known as Lau Pa Sat" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Satay_stalls_along_Boon_Tat_Street_next_to_Telok_Ayer_Market%2C_Singapore_-_20120629-02.jpg/220px-Satay_stalls_along_Boon_Tat_Street_next_to_Telok_Ayer_Market%2C_Singapore_-_20120629-02.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Satay_stalls_along_Boon_Tat_Street_next_to_Telok_Ayer_Market%2C_Singapore_-_20120629-02.jpg/330px-Satay_stalls_along_Boon_Tat_Street_next_to_Telok_Ayer_Market%2C_Singapore_-_20120629-02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Satay_stalls_along_Boon_Tat_Street_next_to_Telok_Ayer_Market%2C_Singapore_-_20120629-02.jpg/440px-Satay_stalls_along_Boon_Tat_Street_next_to_Telok_Ayer_Market%2C_Singapore_-_20120629-02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6000" data-file-height="4000"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Satay_stalls_along_Boon_Tat_Street_next_to_Telok_Ayer_Market,_Singapore_-_20120629-02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Lau_Pa_Sat" title="Lau Pa Sat" class="mw-redirect">Lau Pa Sat</a> 
        <a href="/wiki/Hawker_centre" title="Hawker centre">hawker centre</a> in the midst of the financial district. 
        <a href="/wiki/Satay" title="Satay">Satay</a> cart-stalls rolls in after dusk, on a side street
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Dining, along with shopping, is said to be the country's national pastime.<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">[271]</a></sup> The focus on food has led countries like Australia to attract Singaporean tourists with food-based itineraries.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">[272]</a></sup> The diversity of food is touted as a reason to visit the country,<sup id="cite_ref-Foodways_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Foodways-275">[273]</a></sup> and the variety of food representing different ethnicities is seen by the government as a symbol of its multiculturalism.<sup id="cite_ref-Martini_276-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Martini-276">[274]</a></sup> The "national fruit" of Singapore is the <a href="/wiki/Durian" title="Durian">durian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">[275]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In popular culture, food items belong to a particular ethnicity, with Chinese, Malay, and Indian food clearly defined. However, the diversity of cuisine has been increased further by the "hybridisation" of different styles (e.g., the <a href="/wiki/Peranakan_cuisine" title="Peranakan cuisine">Peranakan cuisine</a>, a mix of Chinese and Malay cuisine).<sup id="cite_ref-Foodways_275-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Foodways-275">[273]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts">Arts</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:The_Esplanade_%E2%80%93_Theatres_on_the_Bay.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Domed performing arts centre with spikes reminiscent of a durian fruit" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/The_Esplanade_%E2%80%93_Theatres_on_the_Bay.jpg/220px-The_Esplanade_%E2%80%93_Theatres_on_the_Bay.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/The_Esplanade_%E2%80%93_Theatres_on_the_Bay.jpg/330px-The_Esplanade_%E2%80%93_Theatres_on_the_Bay.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/The_Esplanade_%E2%80%93_Theatres_on_the_Bay.jpg/440px-The_Esplanade_%E2%80%93_Theatres_on_the_Bay.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1496" data-file-height="991"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:The_Esplanade_%E2%80%93_Theatres_on_the_Bay.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Esplanade performing arts centre, fronting 
        <a href="/wiki/Marina_Bay,_Singapore" title="Marina Bay, Singapore">Marina Bay</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Since the 1990s, the government has been promoting Singapore as a centre for arts and culture, in particular the performing arts, and to transform the country into a cosmopolitan "gateway between the East and West".<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">[276]</a></sup> One highlight was the construction of <a href="/wiki/Esplanade_%E2%80%93_Theatres_on_the_Bay" title="Esplanade – Theatres on the Bay">Esplanade – Theatres on the Bay</a>, a performing arts centre opened in October 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">[277]</a></sup> The national orchestra, <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Singapore Symphony Orchestra">Singapore Symphony Orchestra</a>, plays at the Esplanade. The annual <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Arts_Festival" title="Singapore Arts Festival">Singapore Arts Festival</a> is organised by the National Arts Council. The stand-up comedy scene has been growing, with a weekly <a href="/wiki/Open_mic" title="Open mic">open mic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">[278]</a></sup> Singapore hosted the 2009 <a href="/wiki/Gen%C3%A9e_International_Ballet_Competition" title="Genée International Ballet Competition">Genée International Ballet Competition</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Classical_ballet" title="Classical ballet">classical ballet</a> competition promoted by London's <a href="/wiki/Royal_Academy_of_Dance" title="Royal Academy of Dance">Royal Academy of Dance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">[279]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport_and_recreation">Sport and recreation</span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Singapore" title="Sport in Singapore">Sport in Singapore</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Seating_at_Singapore_National_Stadium.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Seating_at_Singapore_National_Stadium.jpg/220px-Seating_at_Singapore_National_Stadium.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Seating_at_Singapore_National_Stadium.jpg/330px-Seating_at_Singapore_National_Stadium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Seating_at_Singapore_National_Stadium.jpg/440px-Seating_at_Singapore_National_Stadium.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Seating_at_Singapore_National_Stadium.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/National_Stadium,_Singapore" title="National Stadium, Singapore">National Stadium, Singapore</a> at the Sports Hub
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Popular sports include football, basketball, cricket, swimming, sailing, table tennis and badminton. Most Singaporeans live in public residential areas (known as "<a href="/wiki/Public_housing_in_Singapore" title="Public housing in Singapore">HDB flats</a>") near amenities such as public swimming pools, outdoor <a href="/wiki/Basketball_court" title="Basketball court">basketball courts</a> and indoor sport complexes. Water sports are popular, including sailing, <a href="/wiki/Kayaking" title="Kayaking">kayaking</a> and <a href="/wiki/Water_skiing" title="Water skiing">water skiing</a>. <a href="/wiki/Scuba_diving" title="Scuba diving">Scuba diving</a> is another popular recreational sport. The southern island of <a href="/wiki/Pulau_Hantu" title="Pulau Hantu">Pulau Hantu</a>, particularly, is known for its rich <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">coral reefs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">[280]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Singapore's <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> league, the <a href="/wiki/S-League" title="S-League" class="mw-redirect">S-League</a>, launched in 1996,<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">[281]</a></sup> currently comprises 9 clubs, including 2 foreign teams. The <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Slingers" title="Singapore Slingers">Singapore Slingers</a>, formerly the Hunter Pirates in the <a href="/wiki/Australian_National_Basketball_League" title="Australian National Basketball League" class="mw-redirect">Australian National Basketball League</a>, is one of the inaugural teams in the <a href="/wiki/ASEAN_Basketball_League" title="ASEAN Basketball League">ASEAN Basketball League</a> which was founded in October 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">[282]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Singapore began hosting a round of the <a href="/wiki/Formula_One_World_Championship" title="Formula One World Championship" class="mw-redirect">Formula One World Championship</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Grand_Prix" title="Singapore Grand Prix">Singapore Grand Prix</a>, in 2008. The race takes place on the <a href="/wiki/Marina_Bay_Street_Circuit" title="Marina Bay Street Circuit">Marina Bay Street Circuit</a> and was the inaugural F1 night race,<sup id="cite_ref-News_.E2.80.93_Singapore_confirms_2008_night_race_285-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-News_.E2.80.93_Singapore_confirms_2008_night_race-285">[283]</a></sup> and the first F1 street race in Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-1stStreet_286-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1stStreet-286">[284]</a></sup> The Singapore Grand Prix will remain on the F1 calendar through at least 2017, after race organisers signed a contract extension with <a href="/wiki/Formula_One_Group" title="Formula One Group">Formula One Group</a> on the eve of the 2012 event.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">[285]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Kranji_Racecourse" title="Kranji Racecourse">Kranji Racecourse</a> is run by the <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Turf_Club" title="Singapore Turf Club">Singapore Turf Club</a> and hosts multiple weekly meetings and many important local and international races, notably the prestigious <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Airlines_International_Cup" title="Singapore Airlines International Cup">Singapore Airlines International Cup</a>.</p> 
     <p>Singapore also hosted the inaugural <a href="/wiki/2010_Summer_Youth_Olympics" title="2010 Summer Youth Olympics">2010 Summer Youth Olympics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Singapore_to_host_first_edition_of_the_Youth_Olympic_Games_in_2010_288-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Singapore_to_host_first_edition_of_the_Youth_Olympic_Games_in_2010-288">[286]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Singapore" title="Media of Singapore">Media of Singapore</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Companies linked to the government control much of the domestic media in Singapore.<sup id="cite_ref-freedomhouse_a_289-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedomhouse_a-289">[287]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/MediaCorp" title="MediaCorp" class="mw-redirect">MediaCorp</a> operates most <a href="/wiki/Television_in_Singapore" title="Television in Singapore">free-to-air television channels</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_radio_stations_in_Singapore" title="List of radio stations in Singapore">free-to-air radio stations</a> in Singapore. There are a total of seven free-to-air TV channels offered by Mediacorp.<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">[288]</a></sup> The channels are <a href="/wiki/MediaCorp_Channel_5" title="MediaCorp Channel 5" class="mw-redirect">Channel 5 (English channel)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Channel_NewsAsia" title="Channel NewsAsia">Channel News Asia (English channel)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Okto" title="Okto">Okto</a> (English channel), <a href="/wiki/MediaCorp_Channel_8" title="MediaCorp Channel 8" class="mw-redirect">Channel 8 (Chinese channel)</a>, <a href="/wiki/MediaCorp_Channel_U" title="MediaCorp Channel U" class="mw-redirect">Channel U (Chinese channel)</a>, <a href="/wiki/MediaCorp_Suria" title="MediaCorp Suria" class="mw-redirect">Suria (Malay channel)</a> and <a href="/wiki/MediaCorp_Vasantham" title="MediaCorp Vasantham" class="mw-redirect">Vasantham (Indian channel)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">[289]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Starhub" title="Starhub" class="mw-redirect">Starhub</a> Cable Vision (SCV) also offers cable television with channels from all around the world<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">[290]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Singtel" title="Singtel">Singtel</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Mio_TV" title="Mio TV" class="mw-redirect">Mio TV</a> provides an <a href="/wiki/IPTV" title="IPTV">IPTV</a> service.<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">[291]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Press_Holdings" title="Singapore Press Holdings">Singapore Press Holdings</a>, a body with close links to the government, controls most of the newspaper industry in Singapore.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_Media_294-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Media-294">[292]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Singapore's media industry has sometimes been criticised for being too regulated and lacking in freedom by human rights groups such as <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-freedomhouse_a_289-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedomhouse_a-289">[287]</a></sup> In 2014, <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">Reporters Without Borders</a>, a France-based international non-governmental organisation, ranked Singapore 153rd out of 180 nations in its <a href="/wiki/Press_Freedom_Index" title="Press Freedom Index">Press Freedom Index</a>. This was the lowest ranking for Singapore since the inception of this index<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">[293]</a></sup> in 2002. The <a href="/wiki/Media_Development_Authority" title="Media Development Authority">Media Development Authority</a> regulates Singaporean media, claiming to balance the demand for choice and protection against offensive and harmful material.<sup id="cite_ref-Mica_296-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mica-296">[294]</a></sup> Private ownership of TV satellite dishes is banned.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_Media_294-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Media-294">[292]</a></sup> Television is censored, and shows like <i><a href="/wiki/Sex_and_the_City" title="Sex and the City">Sex and the City</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Queer_as_Folk_(UK_TV_series)" title="Queer as Folk (UK TV series)"><i>Queer as Folk</i></a> are banned. There are 3.4&nbsp;million users of the internet in Singapore,<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_Media_294-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Media-294">[292]</a></sup> one of the highest internet penetration rates in the world. The Singapore government does not engage in widespread censoring of the internet,<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">[295]</a></sup> but it maintains a list of one hundred websites (mostly pornographic) that it blocks as a 'symbolic statement of the Singaporean community's stand on harmful and undesirable content on the Internet'.<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">[296]</a></sup> As the block covers only home internet access, users may still visit the blocked websites from their office computers.<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">[297]</a></sup></p>

           <tr> 
            <td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="2" style="padding:0.5em 0 0.3em; line-height:1.3em;"> 
             <div>
              <b>*</b>
              <a href="/wiki/Transcontinental_country" title="Transcontinental country" class="mw-redirect">Transcontinental country</a>.
              <br> 
              <b>†</b> Both Israel and Palestinians 
              <a href="/wiki/Positions_on_Jerusalem" title="Positions on Jerusalem">claim Jerusalem as capital</a>. 
              <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a> contains the Israeli parliament and almost all Israeli government ministries. 
              <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">Tel Aviv</a> contains most foreign embassies in Israel; 
              <a href="/wiki/Ramallah" title="Ramallah">Ramallah</a> is the administrative seat of the Palestinian Authority.
             </div> </td>
